Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Judiciary and Judicial Administration
=======================================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Chapter 1 - Judiciary
*******************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-101 Courts of this state -- Courts of record.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-101(1): The following are the courts of this state:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-101(1)(a): the Supreme Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-101(1)(b): the Court of Appeals;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-101(1)(c): the Business and Chancery Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-101(1)(d): the district courts;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-101(1)(e): the juvenile courts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-101(1)(f): the justice courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-101(2): All courts are courts of record, except the justice courts, which are courts not of record.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102 Trial courts of record -- Geographical divisions.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102(1): The district and juvenile courts are divided into eight geographical divisions:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102(1)(a): First Judicial District, which includes Box Elder, Cache, and Rich Counties;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102(1)(b): Second Judicial District, which includes Weber, Davis, and Morgan Counties;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102(1)(c): Third Judicial District, which includes Salt Lake, Summit, and Tooele Counties;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102(1)(d): Fourth Judicial District, which includes Utah, Wasatch, Juab, and Millard Counties;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102(1)(e): Fifth Judicial District, which includes Beaver, Iron, and Washington Counties;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102(1)(f): Sixth Judicial District, which includes Garfield, Kane, Piute, Sanpete, Sevier, and Wayne Counties;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102(1)(g): Seventh Judicial District, which includes Carbon, Emery, Grand, and San Juan Counties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102(1)(h): Eighth Judicial District, which includes Daggett, Duchesne, and Uintah Counties.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-102(2): The Business and Chancery Court is not divided into geographical divisions.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103 Number of district court judges.
----------------------------------------------------------------
The number of district court judges is:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103(1): four district court judges in the First Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103(2): 14 district court judges in the Second Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103(3): 32 district court judges in the Third Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103(4): 13 district court judges in the Fourth Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103(5): seven district court judges in the Fifth Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103(6): two district court judges in the Sixth Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103(7): three district court judges in the Seventh Judicial District; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103(8): three district court judges in the Eighth Judicial District.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103.5 Number of Business and Chancery Court judges -- Disqualification or recusal of a Business and Chancery Court judge.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103.5(1): The Business and Chancery Court shall consist of one judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103.5(2): If there are fewer than three judges for the Business and Chancery Court under Subsection (1), the presiding officer of the Judicial Council shall designate a pool of two district court judges to preside over actions in the Business and Chancery Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-103.5(3): A district court judge designated under Subsection (2) may preside over an action when each Business and Chancery Court judge is unable to preside over an action due to recusal or disqualification.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-104 Number of juvenile court judges.
----------------------------------------------------------------
The number of juvenile court judges is:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-104(1): two juvenile court judges in the First Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-104(2): six juvenile court judges in the Second Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-104(3): nine juvenile court judges in the Third Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-104(4): seven juvenile court judges in the Fourth Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-104(5): three juvenile court judges in the Fifth Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-104(6): two juvenile court judges in the Sixth Judicial District;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-104(7): two juvenile court judges in the Seventh Judicial District; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-104(8): two juvenile court judges in the Eighth Judicial District.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-105 Merger of district court and circuit court.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-105(1): Effective July 1, 1996, the circuit court shall be merged into the district court.  The district court shall have jurisdiction as provided by law for the district court and shall have jurisdiction over all matters filed in the court formerly denominated the circuit court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-105(2): The district court shall continue the judicial offices, judges, staff, cases, authority, duties, and all other attributes of the court formerly denominated the circuit court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-105(3): Judges of the court formerly denominated the circuit court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-105(3)(a): on July 1, 1996, be judges of the district court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-105(3)(b): next stand for retention election at the first general election held more than three years after their appointment or at the general election held in the sixth year after their last retention election, as applicable.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-1-106 Transition clause -- Recodification of Title 78.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
For purposes of a matter pending in any court beginning February 7, 2008 through August 31, 2008, citation to an appropriate section in the previous

Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Chapter 2 - Judicial Administration
*********************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known and cited as the "Judicial Administration Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-102 Purpose.
----------------------------------------
The purpose of this chapter is to create an administrative system for all courts of this state, subject to central direction by the Judicial Council, to enable these courts to provide uniformity and coordination in the administration of justice.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-103 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-103(1): 78A-2-111 "Conference" means the annual statewide judicial conference established by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-103(2): "Council" means the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-103(3): "Courts" mean all courts of this state, including all courts of record and not of record.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-103(4): "Judicial Council" means the Judicial Council established by


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104 Judicial Council -- Creation -- Members -- Terms and election -- Responsibilities -- Reports -- Guardian Ad Litem Oversight Committee.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(1): The Judicial Council is composed of:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(1)(a): the chief justice of the Supreme Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(1)(b): one member elected by the justices of the Supreme Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(1)(c): one member elected by the judges of the Court of Appeals;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(1)(d): one member elected by the judges of the Business and Chancery Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(1)(e): six members elected by the judges of the district courts;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(1)(f): three members elected by the judges of the juvenile courts;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(1)(g): three members elected by the justice court judges; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(1)(h): a member or ex officio member of the Board of Commissioners of the Utah State Bar who is an active member of the Utah State Bar in good standing at the time of election by the Board of Commissioners.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(2): The Judicial Council shall have a seal.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(3)(a): The chief justice of the Supreme Court shall act as presiding officer of the Judicial Council and chief administrative officer for the courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(3)(b): The chief justice shall vote only in the case of a tie.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(4): (1)(h); (1)(h)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(4)(a): All members of the Judicial Council shall serve for three-year terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(4)(b): If a Judicial Council member should die, resign, retire, or otherwise fail to complete a term of office, the appropriate constituent group shall elect a member to complete the term of office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(4)(c): In courts having more than one member, the members shall be elected to staggered terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(4)(d): (1)(h) The individual elected by the Board of Commissioners under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(4)(e): (1)(h) The individual elected by the Board of Commissioners under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(4)(f): Elections are held under rules made by the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(5)(a): The Judicial Council is responsible for the development of uniform administrative policy for the courts throughout the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(5)(b): The presiding officer of the Judicial Council is responsible for the implementation of the policies developed by the Judicial Council and for the general management of the courts, with the aid of the state court administrator.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(5)(c): The Judicial Council has authority and responsibility to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(5)(c)(i): establish and assure compliance with policies for the operation of the courts, including uniform rules and forms; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(5)(c)(ii): publish and submit to the governor, the chief justice of the Supreme Court, and the Legislature an annual report of the operations of the courts, which shall include financial and statistical data and may include suggestions and recommendations for legislation.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(6): The Judicial Council shall establish standards for the operation of the courts of the state, including facilities, court security, support services, and staff levels for judicial and support personnel.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(7): The Judicial Council shall by rule:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(7)(a): establish the time and manner for destroying court records, including computer records; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(7)(b): establish retention periods for court records.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(8): 41-1a-407
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(8)(a): Consistent with the requirements of judicial office and security policies, the Judicial Council shall establish procedures to govern the assignment of state vehicles to public officers of the judicial branch.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(8)(b): 41-1a-407 The vehicles shall be marked in a manner consistent with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(9)(a): The Judicial Council shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(9)(a)(i): advise judicial officers and employees concerning ethical issues; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(9)(a)(ii): establish procedures for issuing informal and formal advisory opinions on ethical issues.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(9)(b): Compliance with an informal opinion is evidence of good faith compliance with the Code of Judicial Conduct.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(9)(c): A formal opinion constitutes a binding interpretation of the Code of Judicial Conduct.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(11)(b): There shall be at least one court clerk's office open during regular court hours in each county.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(11)(c): Any trial court of record may hold court in any municipality designated as a location of a court of record.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-104(12): The Judicial Council shall by rule determine whether the administration of a court is the obligation of the Administrative Office of the Courts or whether the Administrative Office of the Courts should contract with local government for court support services.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-105 State court administrator -- Appointment -- Qualifications -- Salary.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Supreme Court shall appoint a chief administrative officer of the council who shall have the title of the state court administrator and shall serve at the pleasure of the council, the Supreme Court, or both.  The state court administrator shall be selected on the basis of professional ability and experience in the field of public administration and shall possess an understanding of court procedures as well as of the nature and significance of other court services. The state court administrator shall devote the state court administrator's full time and attention to the duties of the state court administrator's office, and shall receive a salary equal to that of a district court judge.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-106 Presiding officer -- Compensation -- Duties.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-106(1): The chief justice of the Supreme Court shall serve as the presiding officer of the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-106(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-106(2)(a): The presiding officer of the Judicial Council shall supervise the courts to ensure uniform adherence to law and to the rules and forms adopted by the council and to promote the proper and efficient functioning of the courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-106(2)(b): The presiding officer of the council may issue orders as necessary to assure compliance with uniform administrative practices.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-107(1)(f): assist justice courts in budgetary, fiscal, and accounting procedures;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-107(1)(g): conduct studies of the business of the courts, including the preparation of recommendations and reports relating to the studies;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-107(1)(h): develop uniform procedures for the management of court business, including the management of court calendars;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-107(1)(i): maintain liaison with the governmental and other public and private groups having an interest in the administration of the courts;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-107(1)(j): establish uniform policy concerning vacations and sick leave for judges and nonjudicial officers of the courts;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-107(1)(k): establish uniform hours for court sessions throughout the state;

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-108 Assistants for state court administrator -- Appointment of trial court executives.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-108(1): The state court administrator, with the approval of the presiding officer of the Judicial Council, is responsible for the establishment of positions and salaries of assistants as necessary to enable the state court administrator to perform the powers and duties vested in the state court administrator by this chapter, including the positions of appellate court administrator, business and chancery court administrator, district court administrator, juvenile court administrator, and justice court administrator.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-108(2): The state court administrator shall appoint an appellate court administrator, a business and chancery court administrator, a district court administrator, a juvenile court administrator, and a justice court administrator with the concurrence of the respective boards as established by the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-108(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-108(3)(a): The district court administrator, with the concurrence of the presiding judge of a district or the district court judge in single judge districts, may appoint a trial court executive in each district.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-108(3)(b): The trial court executive may appoint, subject to budget limitations, necessary support personnel including clerks, research clerks, secretaries, and other persons required to carry out the work of the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-108(3)(c): The trial court executive shall supervise the work of all nonjudicial court staff and serve as administrative officer of the district.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-108(4): Administrators and assistants appointed under this section are known collectively as the Administrative Office of the Courts.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-109 Courts to provide information and statistical data to state court administrator.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The judges, clerks of the courts, and all other officers, state and local, shall comply with all requests made by the state court administrator or the state court administrator's assistants for information and statistical data bearing on the state of the dockets of the courts and such other information as may reflect the business transacted by them and the expenditure of public money for the maintenance and operation of the judicial system.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110 Databases for judicial boards.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(1): As used in this section, "judicial board" means any judicial branch board, commission, council, committee, working group, task force, study group, advisory group, or other body with a defined limited membership that is created to operate for more than six months by:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(1)(a): the constitution;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(1)(b): statute;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(1)(c): judicial order;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(1)(d): any justice or judge;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(1)(e): the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(1)(f): the state court administrator, a district court administrator, trial court executive, or a business and chancery court administrator; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(1)(g): any clerk or administrator in the judicial branch of state government.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(2): The Judicial Council shall designate an individual from the Judicial Council's staff to maintain a computerized database containing information about all judicial boards.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3): (3)(d) The individual designated to maintain the database shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a): ensure that the database contains:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(i): the name of the judicial board;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(ii): the statutory or constitutional authority for the creation of the judicial board;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(iii): the court or other judicial entity under whose jurisdiction the judicial board operates or with which the judicial board is affiliated, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(iv): the name, address, gender, telephone number, and county of each individual currently serving on the judicial board, along with a notation of all vacant or unfilled positions;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(v): the title of the position held by the individual who appointed each member of the judicial board;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(vi): the length of the term to which each member of the judicial board was appointed and the month and year that each judicial board member's term expires;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(vii): the organization, interest group, profession, local government entity, or geographic area that the member of the judicial board represents, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(viii): whether or not the judicial board allocates state or federal funds and the amount of those funds allocated during the last fiscal year;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(ix): whether the judicial board is a policy board or an advisory board;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(x): whether or not the judicial board has or exercises rulemaking authority; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(a)(xi): any compensation and expense reimbursement that members of the executive board are authorized to receive;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(b): make the information contained in the database available to the public upon request;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(c): cooperate with other entities of state government to publish the data or useful summaries of the data;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(d): prepare, publish, and distribute an annual report by April 1 of each year that includes, as of March 1 of that year:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(d)(i): the total number of judicial boards;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(d)(ii): the name of each of those judicial boards and the court, council, administrator, executive, or clerk under whose jurisdiction the executive board operates or with which the judicial board is affiliated, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(d)(iii): for each court, council, administrator, executive, or clerk, the total number of judicial boards under the jurisdiction of or affiliated with that court, council, administrator, executive, or clerk;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(d)(iv): the total number of members for each of those judicial boards;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(d)(v): whether each board is a policymaking board or an advisory board and the total number of policy boards and the total number of advisory boards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(d)(vi): the compensation, if any, paid to the members of each of those judicial boards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-110(3)(e): (3)(d) distribute copies of the report described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-111 Annual judicial conference.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-111(1): There is established an annual judicial conference for all courts of this state, to facilitate the exchange of ideas among all courts and judges, and to study and improve the administration of the courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-111(2): All elections provided in this act shall be conducted during the annual judicial conference.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-112 Grants to nonprofit legal assistance organization.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Subject to legislative appropriation, the state court administrator shall, in accordance withUtah Code Annotated § 78A-2-112(1): low to moderate income victims of domestic violence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-112(2): low to moderate income individuals in family law matters.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113 Judicial hiring freeze authorized.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113(1): As used in this section, "General Fund budget deficit" means a situation where General Fund appropriations made by the Legislature for a fiscal year exceed the estimated revenues adopted by the Executive Appropriations Committee of the Legislature for the General Fund in that fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113(2): (2)(a); (d) During a General Fund budget deficit, the governor, president of the Senate, speaker of the House, and chief justice of the Supreme Court, may, by unanimous vote, implement a judicial hiring freeze for judicial vacancies for:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113(2)(a): a juvenile court district with three or more juvenile court judges;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113(2)(b): a district court district with three or more district court judges;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113(2)(c): all Business and Chancery Court judges;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113(2)(d): all appellate court judges; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113(2)(e): (2)(a); (d) any combination of Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113(3): In implementing a judicial hiring freeze, the governor, president of the Senate, speaker of the House, and chief justice of the Supreme Court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113(3)(a): establish the length of that hiring freeze; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-113(3)(b): ensure that the hiring freeze lasts at least 90 days, but not longer than the last day of the annual general session of the Legislature.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201 Powers of every court.
------------------------------------------------------
Every court has authority to:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201(1): preserve and enforce order in its immediate presence;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201(2): enforce order in the proceedings before it, or before a person authorized to conduct a judicial investigation under its authority;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201(3): provide for the orderly conduct of proceedings before it or its officers;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201(4): compel obedience to its judgments, orders, and process, and to the orders of a judge out of court, in a pending action or proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201(5): control in furtherance of justice the conduct of its ministerial officers, and of all other persons in any manner connected with a judicial proceeding before it in every matter;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201(6): compel the attendance of persons to testify in a pending action or proceeding, as provided by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201(7): administer oaths in a pending action or proceeding, and in all other cases where necessary in the exercise of its authority and duties;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201(8): amend and control its process and orders to conform to law and justice;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201(9): devise and make new process and forms of proceedings, consistent with law, necessary to carry into effect its authority and jurisdiction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-201(10): enforce rules of the Supreme Court and Judicial Council.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-202 Authority of court.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-202(1): A court of this state has the authority necessary to exercise the court's jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-202(2): If a procedure for an action is not established, a process may be adopted that conforms with the apparent intent of the statute or rule of procedure.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-203 Rules -- Right to make -- Limitation -- Security.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-203(1): Every court of record may make rules, not inconsistent with law, for its own government and the government of its officers; but such rules must neither impose any tax or charge upon any legal proceeding nor give any allowance to any officer for service.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-203(2): 76-8-311.1; (2)(a); (2)(b)(i); (2)(b)(i)

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-203(2)(b): (2)(a); (2)(b)(i); (2)(b)(i)

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-203.5 Submission of court rules or proposed court rules.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
When the Supreme Court or Judicial Council submits a court rule or proposal for court rule for public comment, the Supreme Court or Judicial Council shall submit the court rule or proposal for court rule to publication houses that publish court rules, proposals to court rules, case law, or other relevant information for individuals engaged in the legal profession.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-204 Judicial Council to approve court seals.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Judicial Council shall approve a seal for all courts of this state.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-205 When seal is affixed.
-----------------------------------------------------
The seal of the court need not be affixed to any document of the court, except to:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-205(1): a writ;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-205(2): a certificate of the probate of a will, or of appointment of an executor, administrator, or guardian; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-205(3): the authentication of:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-205(3)(a): a copy of a record or document on file with the court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-205(3)(b): the signature of an officer of the court.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-206 English language for proceedings.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Judicial proceedings shall be conducted in the English language.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-207 Domestic relations cases -- Party designation.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Parties in domestic relations cases, including divorce, annulment, property division, child custody, support, parent-time, adoption, and paternity, shall be designated as petitioner and respondent.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-208 Sittings of courts -- To be public -- Notice to public of recording -- Right to exclude in certain cases.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-208(1): (3); (4) The sittings of every court of this state are public, except as provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-208(2): The Judicial Council shall require that notice be given to the public that the proceedings are being recorded when an electronic or digital recording system is being used during court proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-208(3): The court may, in the court's discretion, during the examination of a witness exclude any and all other witnesses in the proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-208(4): In an action of divorce, criminal conversation, seduction, abortion, rape, or assault with intent to commit rape, the court may, in the court's discretion, exclude all persons who do not have a direct interest in the proceedings, except jurors, witnesses and officers of the court.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-209 Sheriff to supply court rooms when the county legislative body neglects.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If suitable rooms for holding the district court and for chambers of the judge are not provided in the place appointed for holding court in any county, together with attendants, furniture, lights, and stationery sufficient for the transaction of business, the court or the judge may direct the sheriff to provide rooms, attendants, furniture, fuel, lights, and stationery.  All expenses incurred, certified by the judge to be correct, are a charge against the county and shall be paid out of the county's general fund.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-210 Change of place of trial because of calamity.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-210(1): The presiding judge may order court proceedings to be held at another location within the jurisdiction if the presiding judge determines it is necessary because of:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-210(1)(a): war;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-210(1)(b): insurrection;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-210(1)(c): pestilence;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-210(1)(d): public calamity or natural disaster; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-210(1)(e): destruction of or danger to the building in which court is held.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-210(2): Any order to move court proceedings shall be reduced to writing and filed with the clerk of the court for publication.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-211 Court days.
-------------------------------------------
All courts of this state are open and judicial business may be transacted on any day, except as provided in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-212 Days on which court closed -- Exceptions.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Judicial business on Sunday, on any day on which a regular general election is held, or on any legal holiday, is limited to the following purposes:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-212(1): to give, upon their request, instructions to a jury when deliberating on the jury's verdict;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-212(2): to receive a verdict or discharge a jury;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-212(3): for the exercise of the powers of a magistrate in a criminal action, or in a proceeding of a criminal nature; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-212(4): judicial business not involving a trial or hearing unless the judge finds it necessary for the fair administration of justice.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-213 Proceedings unaffected by vacancy in office of judge.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
No proceeding in any court of this state is affected by a vacancy in the office of all or any of the judges or by the failure of a term of a judge.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-214 Collection of accounts receivable.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-214(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-214(1)(a): "Accounts receivable" means any amount due the state from an entity for which payment has not been received by the state agency that is servicing the debt.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-214(1)(b): "Accounts receivable" includes unpaid fees, licenses, taxes, loans, overpayments, fines, forfeitures, surcharges, costs, contracts, interest, penalties, restitution to victims, third party claims, sale of goods, sale of services, claims, and damages.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-214(2): If a defendant is sentenced before July 1, 2021, and the Department of Corrections, or the Office of State Debt Collection, is not responsible for collecting an accounts receivable for the defendant, the district court shall collect the accounts receivable for the defendant.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-214(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-214(3)(a): In the juvenile court, money collected by the court from past-due accounts receivable may be used to offset system, administrative, legal, and other costs of collection.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-214(3)(b): The juvenile court shall allocate money collected above the cost of collection on a pro rata basis to the various revenue types that generated the accounts receivable.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-214(4): 63A-3-502; 15-1-4 The interest charge described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-215 Abbreviations and numerals.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Common abbreviations may be used, and numbers may be expressed by customary figures or numerals in court documents.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216 Fees for writ of garnishment -- Single or continuing.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(1): Any creditor who serves or causes to be served a writ of garnishment upon the garnishee shall pay to the garnishee:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(1)(a): $10 for a single garnishment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(1)(b): $25 for a continuing garnishment.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(2): The creditor shall pay the fee directly to the garnishee.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(3): If a plaintiff attempts to garnish the property of a person other than the defendant by serving a garnishment on a garnishee, that person may recover from the plaintiff an amount not to exceed $1,000 if the person demonstrates to the court that the plaintiff failed to exercise reasonable diligence in determining that the person and defendant were the same individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(4): The following factors may be taken into consideration by the court in determining whether the plaintiff exercised reasonable diligence in determining whether the person garnished and the defendant were the same individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(4)(a): similarities between the person and the actual judgment debtor, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(4)(a)(i): the spelling of each person's name;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(4)(a)(ii): addresses;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(4)(a)(iii): physical descriptions;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(4)(a)(iv): identifying information, including Social Security number or driver license number; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(4)(a)(v): family status;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(4)(b): whether previous contact was made to determine whether the person was the judgment debtor;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(4)(c): how the determination of who the judgment debtor was, was made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(4)(d): what information the plaintiff had access to or was provided with regarding the actual judgment debtor from all available sources.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(5): An employer who receives a written request for verification of employment, which includes a copy of the judgment and judgment information statement, shall provide verification within 10 days.  The response shall indicate whether or not the defendant identified in the documentation is a current employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-216(6): (3) A plaintiff is not liable for a violation of Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-218 Powers of every judicial officer -- Contempt.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Every judicial officer has power:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-218(1): to preserve and enforce order in his immediate presence, and in proceedings before him, when he is engaged in the performance of official duty;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-218(2): to compel obedience to his lawful orders as provided by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-218(3): to compel the attendance of persons to testify in a proceeding before him in the cases and manner provided by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-218(4): to administer oaths to persons in a proceeding pending before him, and in all other cases where it may be necessary in the exercise of his powers and duties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-218(5): (1); (4) punish for contempt as provided by law to enforce compliance with Subsections


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-219 Powers of judge contradistinguished from court.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A judge may exercise out of court all the powers expressly conferred upon a judge as contradistinguished from the court.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-221 Justices and judges -- Limitations during terms.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A justice or judge of any court of record may not, during his term of office:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-221(1): practice law or have a partner engaged in the practice of law;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-221(2): hold office in or make any contribution to any political party or organization engaged in political activity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-221(3): use, in his efforts to obtain or retain judicial office, any political party designation, reference, or description.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-222 Disqualification for interest or relation to parties.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-222(1): Except by consent of all parties, a justice, judge, or justice court judge may not sit or act in any action or proceeding:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-222(1)(a): to which he is a party, or in which he is interested;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-222(1)(b): when he is related to either party by consanguinity or affinity within the third degree, computed according to the rules of the common law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-222(1)(c): when he has been attorney or counsel for either party in the action or proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-222(2): The provisions of this section  do not apply to the arrangement of the calendar or the regulation of the order of business, nor to the power of transferring the action or proceeding to some other court.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-223 Decisions to be rendered within two months -- Procedures for decisions not rendered.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-223(1): A trial court judge shall decide all matters submitted for final determination within two months of submission, unless circumstances causing the delay are beyond the judge's personal control.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-223(2): The Judicial Council shall establish reporting procedures for all matters not decided within two months of final submission.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-225 Judge of court of record -- Service in other division or court.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A judge of a court of record may serve temporarily as a judge in another geographic division or in another court of record, in accordance with the Utah Constitution and the rules of the Judicial Council.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-226 Repeated application for orders forbidden -- Disobedience -- Contempt.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-226(1): If an application for an order, made to a judge of a court in which the action or proceeding is pending, is refused in whole or in part or is granted conditionally, a subsequent application for the same order may not be made to any other judge, except of a higher court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-226(2): This section does not apply to motions refused for any informality in the papers or proceedings necessary to obtain the order, or to motions refused with liberty to renew them.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-226(3): A notice of appeal for a trial de novo is not a subsequent application for the same order.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-226(4): (1) A violation of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-229 Documents provided to pro se litigants.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-229(1): 63G-2-202(7) Documents classified as private, protected, or sealed by court rule and are provided to a pro se litigant in the course of an action or in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-229(2): Pro se litigants shall be advised by the court that  private, protected, or sealed documents received by the party that the party would not have received but for the litigation and pro se representation are confidential and may not be distributed outside the parties or the court without prior authorization by the court.  A court's failure to give this notice may not be used as a defense to prosecution for a violation of the disclosure rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-229(3): Violation of this section is:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-229(3)(a): punishable by contempt if distribution or release occurs before a final determination is made by the court and the court still has jurisdiction over the parties; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-229(3)(b): a class B misdemeanor if the litigation has been concluded and the court no longer has jurisdiction over the parties.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-230 References to court pleadings and other papers.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any reference in this code to a petition, complaint, or other court record shall be considered to include any cover sheet or accompanying document required by statute or court rule to be filed with the petition, complaint, or other record.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232 Child abuse and domestic abuse education and training for judges, court commissioners, and court personnel.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(1): 77-38-403; 78B-7-102 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(1)(a): 77-38-403 "Advocacy services provider" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(1)(b): 78B-7-102 "Child custody proceeding" means a civil proceeding between the parents of a child that involves the care or custody of the child including proceedings involving:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(1)(b)(i): divorce;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(1)(b)(ii): separation;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(1)(b)(iii): parent-time;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(1)(b)(iv): paternity;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(1)(b)(v): child support;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(1)(b)(vi): legal or physical custody of a child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(1)(b)(vii): 78B-7-102 a civil protective order as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2): 78A-2-105 The state court administrator described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(a): shall be designed to improve the ability of the courts to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(a)(i): recognize domestic violence and child abuse in child custody proceedings; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(a)(ii): make appropriate custody decisions that prioritize a child's physical and psychological safety and well-being;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(b): shall focus solely on domestic and sexual violence and child abuse, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(b)(i): child sexual abuse;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(b)(ii): physical abuse;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(b)(iii): emotional abuse;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(b)(iv): coercive control;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(b)(v): implicit and explicit bias, including biases relating to parents with disabilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(b)(vi): trauma;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(b)(vii): long-term and short-term impacts of domestic violence and child abuse on children; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(b)(viii): victim and perpetrator behavior patterns and relationship dynamics within the cycle of violence;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(c): shall be based on evidence-based and peer-reviewed research by recognized experts in the types of abuse described in Subsection (2)(b);
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(d): shall require training to be provided by a professional with substantial experience in assisting survivors of domestic violence or child abuse, including an advocacy services provider;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(e): may include input from a survivor of domestic violence or child physical or sexual abuse; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(2)(f): may incorporate curriculum, best practices, or other materials developed for or used in similar training and education programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(3)(a): The state court administrator shall present the proposed or recommended training and education program to the Judiciary Interim Committee on or before the committee's September 2024 interim meeting.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(3)(b): The presentation described in Subsection (3)(a) shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(3)(b)(i): recommendations for the specific personnel positions that will be required to participate in the program;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(3)(b)(ii): recommended performance metrics for the program and how those metrics may be tracked;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(3)(b)(iii): an estimate of the costs to implement the program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-232(3)(b)(iv): an identification of potential grant sources, if any, that may be available to fund the program in whole or in part.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302 Indigent litigants -- Affidavit.
----------------------------------------------------------------
I, (insert name), do solemnly swear or affirm that due to my poverty I am unable to bear the expenses of the action or legal proceedings which I am about to commence or the appeal which I am about to take, and that I believe I am entitled to the relief sought by the action, legal proceedings, or appeal.Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1): 78A-2-302; 78A-2-309 As used in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1)(a): "Convicted" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1)(a)(i): a conviction by entry of a plea of guilty or nolo contendere, guilty with a mental condition, no contest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1)(a)(ii): a conviction of any crime or offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1)(b): "Indigent" means an individual who is financially unable to pay fees and costs or give security.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1)(c): "Prisoner" means an individual who has been convicted of a crime and is incarcerated for that crime or is being held in custody for trial or sentencing.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(2): An individual may institute, prosecute, defend, or appeal any cause in a court in this state without prepayment of fees and costs or security if the individual submits an affidavit demonstrating that the individual is indigent.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3): A court shall find an individual indigent if the individual's affidavit under Subsection (2) demonstrates:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(a): for a cause that is not a petition for expungement, the individual has an income level at or below 150% of the United States poverty level, as defined by the most recent poverty income guidelines published by the United States Department of Health and Human Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(b): for a cause that is a petition for expungement:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(b)(i): if the individual has a household size of one, two, or three, the individual has an income level at or below 150% of the United States poverty level for a household size of three, as defined by the most recent poverty income guidelines published by the United States Department of Health and Human Services; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(b)(ii): if the individual has a household size of four or more, the individual has an income level at or below 150% of the United States poverty level for that individual's household size, as defined by the most recent poverty income guidelines published by the United States Department of Health and Human Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(c): the individual receives benefits from a means-tested government program, including Temporary Assistance to Needy Families, Supplemental Security Income, the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program, or Medicaid;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(d): the individual receives legal services from a nonprofit provider or a pro bono attorney through the Utah State Bar; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(e): the individual has insufficient income or other means to pay the necessary fees and costs or security without depriving the individual, or the individual's family, of food, shelter, clothing, or other necessities.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4): An affidavit demonstrating that an individual is indigent under Subsection (3)(e) shall contain complete information on the individual's:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(a): identity and residence;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(b): amount of income, including any government financial support, alimony, or child support;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(c): assets owned, including real and personal property;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(d): business interests;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(e): accounts receivable;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(f): securities, checking and savings account balances;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(g): debts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(h): monthly expenses.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(5): 78A-2-305 If the individual under Subsection (3) is a prisoner, the prisoner shall disclose the amount of money held in the prisoner's trust account at the time the affidavit under Subsection (2) is executed in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(6): An affidavit of indigency under this section shall state the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(7): The Administrative Office of the Courts shall include on a form for an affidavit of indigency the following warning: "It is a crime for anyone to intentionally or knowingly provide false or misleading information to the court when seeking a waiver of a court fee."


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302 Waiver of fees, costs, and security -- Indigent litigants -- Affidavit.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
I, (insert name), do solemnly swear or affirm that due to my poverty I am unable to bear the expenses of the action or legal proceedings which I am about to commence or the appeal which I am about to take, and that I believe I am entitled to the relief sought by the action, legal proceedings, or appeal.Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1): 78A-2-302; 78A-2-309 As used in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1)(a): "Convicted" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1)(a)(i): a conviction by entry of a plea of guilty or nolo contendere, guilty with a mental condition, no contest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1)(a)(ii): a conviction of any crime or offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1)(b): "Indigent" means a financial status that results from a court finding that a petitioner is financially unable to pay the fee, a cost, or give security.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(1)(c): "Prisoner" means an individual who has been convicted of a crime and is incarcerated for that crime or is being held in custody for trial or sentencing.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(2): 77-40a-305 An individual may institute, prosecute, defend, or appeal any cause in a court in this state without prepayment of fees and costs or security if  :
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(2)(a): the individual submits an affidavit demonstrating that the individual is indigent; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(2)(b): 77-40a-305 the cause is a petition for expungement and the individual provides the court with proof that another court granted a waiver of the fee for a petition for expungement as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3): A court shall find an individual indigent if the individual's affidavit under Subsection (2) demonstrates:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(a): for a cause that is not a petition for expungement, the individual has an income level at or below 150% of the United States poverty level as defined by the most recent poverty income guidelines published by the United States Department of Health and Human Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(b): for a cause that is a petition for expungement:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(b)(i): if the individual has a household size of one, two, or three, the individual has an income level at or below 150% of the United States poverty level for a household size of three, as defined by the most recent poverty income guidelines published by the United States Department of Health and Human Services; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(b)(ii): if the individual has a household size of four or more, the individual has an income level at or below 150% of the United States poverty level for that individual's household size, as defined by the most recent poverty income guidelines published by the United States Department of Health and Human Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(c): the individual receives benefits from a means-tested government program, including Temporary Assistance to Needy Families, Supplemental Security Income, the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program, or Medicaid;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(d): the individual receives legal services from a nonprofit provider or a pro bono attorney through the Utah State Bar; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(3)(e): the individual has insufficient income or other means to pay the necessary fees and costs or security without depriving the individual, or the individual's family, of food, shelter, clothing, or other necessities.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4): An affidavit demonstrating that an individual is indigent under Subsection (3)(e) shall contain complete information on the individual's:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(a): identity and residence;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(b): amount of income, including any government financial support, alimony, or child support;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(c): assets owned, including real and personal property;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(d): business interests;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(e): accounts receivable;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(f): securities, checking and savings account balances;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(g): debts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(4)(h): monthly expenses.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(5): 78A-2-305 If the individual under Subsection (3) is a prisoner, the prisoner shall disclose the amount of money held in the prisoner's trust account at the time the affidavit under Subsection (2) is executed in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(6): An affidavit of indigency under this section shall state the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-302(7): The Administrative Office of the Courts shall include on a form for an affidavit of indigency the following warning: "It is a crime for anyone to intentionally or knowingly provide false or misleading information to the court when seeking a waiver of a court fee."


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303 False affidavit -- Penalty.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(1): 78A-2-302 An individual may assert by affidavit that an affidavit of indigency under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(1)(a): false;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(1)(b): frivolous or without merit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(1)(c): malicious.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(2): (1) Upon receipt of an affidavit in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(2)(a): post a bond for the costs of the action or appeal; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(2)(b): pay the legal fees for the action or appeal.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(3): The court may dismiss the action or appeal if:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(3)(a): the affiant does not appear;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(3)(b): the affiant appears and the court determines the affidavit is false, frivolous, without merit, or malicious; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-303(3)(c): the court orders the affiant to post a bond or pay the legal fees and the affiant fails to do so.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304 Effect of filing affidavit -- Nonprisoner.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304(1): 78A-2-302
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304(1)(a): 78A-2-302 Upon the filing of an affidavit of indigency under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304(1)(b): Notwithstanding the party's statement of inability to pay court costs, the court shall require a partial or full filing fee where the financial information provided demonstrates an ability to pay a fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304(2)(a): In instances where fees or costs are completely waived, the court shall immediately file any complaint or papers on appeal and do what is necessary or proper as promptly as if the litigant had fully paid all the regular fees.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304(2)(b): The constable or sheriff shall immediately serve any summonses, writs, process and subpoenas, and papers necessary or proper in the prosecution or defense of the cause, for the indigent individual as if all the necessary fees and costs had been fully paid.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304(3): 78A-2-302
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304(3)(a): 78A-2-302 In cases where an affidavit of indigency under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304(3)(b): If the court opines that the individual is reasonably able to pay the costs, the court shall direct the judgment or decree not be entered in favor of that individual until the costs are paid.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-304(3)(c): The order may be cancelled later upon petition if the facts warrant cancellation.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305 Effect of filing affidavit -- Procedure for review and collection.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(1): 78A-2-302
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(1)(a): 78A-2-302 Upon receipt of an affidavit of indigency under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(1)(b): The incarcerating facility shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(1)(b)(i): prepare and produce to the court the prisoner's six-month trust account statement, current trust account balance, and aggregate disposable income; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(1)(b)(ii): calculate aggregate disposable income by totaling all deposits made in the prisoner's trust account during the six-month period and subtracting all funds automatically deducted or otherwise garnished from the account during the same period.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(2): The court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(2)(a): review both the affidavit of indigency and the financial account statement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(2)(b): based upon the review, independently determine whether or not the prisoner is financially capable of paying all the regular fees and costs associated with filing the action.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(3): When the court concludes that the prisoner is unable to pay full fees and costs, the court shall assess an initial partial filing fee equal to 50% of the prisoner's current trust account balance or 10% of the prisoner's six-month aggregate disposable income, whichever is greater.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(4)(a): After payment of the initial partial filing fee, the court shall require the prisoner to make monthly payments of 20% of the preceding month's aggregate disposable income until the regular filing fee associated with the civil action is paid in full.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(4)(b): The agency having custody of the prisoner shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(4)(b)(i): garnish the prisoner's account each month; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(4)(b)(ii): once the collected fees exceed $10, forward payments to the clerk of the court until the filing fees are paid.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(4)(c): Nothing in this section may be construed to prevent the agency having custody of the prisoner from withdrawing funds from the prisoner's account to pay court-ordered restitution.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(5): Collection of the filing fees continues despite dismissal of the action.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(6): The filing fee collected may not exceed the amount of fees permitted by statute for the commencement of a civil action or an appeal of a civil action.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7): 78A-2-302; (7)(c)(ii) If the prisoner is filing an initial divorce action or an action to obtain custody of the prisoner's children, the following procedures shall apply for review and collection of fees and costs:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7)(a): 78A-2-302
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7)(a)(i): 78A-2-302 Upon a filing of an affidavit of indigency under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7)(a)(ii): The court shall require a full or partial filing fee when the prisoner's financial information demonstrates an ability to pay the applicable court fees or costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7)(b)(i): If a prisoner's court fees or costs are completely waived, and if the prisoner files an appeal, the court shall immediately file any complaint or papers on appeal and complete all necessary action as promptly as if the litigant had paid all the fees and costs in full.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7)(b)(ii): If a prisoner is indigent, the constable and sheriff shall immediately serve any summonses, writs, process and subpoenas, and papers necessary in the prosecution or defense of the cause as if all the necessary fees and costs had been paid in full.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7)(c): (7)(c)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7)(c)(i): If a prisoner files an affidavit of indigency, the judge shall question the prisoner at the time of the hearing on the merits of the case as to the prisoner's ability to pay.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7)(c)(ii): If the judge determines that the prisoner is reasonably able to pay court fees and costs, the final order or decree shall be entered, however the prisoner may not seek enforcement or modification of the decree or order until the prisoner has paid the fees or costs in full.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-305(7)(c)(iii): (7)(c)(ii) A judge may waive the restrictions placed on the prisoner in Subsection

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-306(1)(a): the initial filing fee required as a prerequisite to proceeding with the action;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-306(1)(b): 78A-2-307 the procedure available to challenge the initial filing fee assessment as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-306(1)(c): the prisoner's ongoing obligation to make monthly payments until the entire filing fee is paid.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-307 Filing fee challenge -- Court powers.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-307(1): 78A-2-306 Within 10 days of receiving court notice requiring an initial filing fee under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-307(2): The court shall review the memorandum and supporting documents challenging the fee assessment for facial validity.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-307(3): The court may reduce the initial filing fee, authorize service of process, or otherwise proceed with the action without prepayment of costs and fees if the memorandum shows the litigant:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-307(3)(a): has lost his source of income;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-307(3)(b): has unaccounted nondiscretionary expenses limiting his ability to pay;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-307(3)(c): will suffer immediate irreparable harm if the action is unnecessarily delayed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-307(3)(d): will otherwise lose the cause of action by unnecessary delays associated with securing funds necessary to satisfy the assessed filing fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-307(4): Nothing in this section shall be construed to relieve the litigant from the ongoing obligation of monthly payments until the filing fee is paid in full.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-308 Failure to serve papers -- Penalty.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Any justice court judge, clerk, or officer refusing to file or serve the papers is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-309 Liability for fees if successful in litigation.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-309(1): Nothing in this part shall prevent a justice court judge, clerk, constable, or sheriff from collecting regular fees for all services rendered for the indigent individual, in the event the indigent individual is successful in litigation.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-309(2): All fees and costs shall be regularly taxed and included in any judgment recovered by the indigent individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-309(3): The fees and costs shall be paid to a justice court judge, clerk, constable, or sheriff.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-309(4): If the indigent individual fails in the action or appeal, the costs of the action or appeal may be adjudged against the indigent individual.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310 Report by Judicial Council on court fees.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(1)(a): "Cost" means the direct and indirect costs and expenses for providing the good or service for which a fee is charged, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(1)(a)(i): salaries, benefits, contracted labor costs, travel expenses, training expenses, equipment and material costs, depreciation expenses, utility costs, and other overhead costs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(1)(a)(ii): costs and expenses for administering the fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(1)(b)(i): "Judiciary" means the Judicial Council, the Supreme Court, the Court of Appeals, a district court, or a juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(1)(b)(ii): "Judiciary" includes any board, committee, or staff office of the Judicial Council, the Supreme Court, the Court of Appeals, a district court, or a juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(2): Before November 30 of each year, the Judicial Council shall submit a report to the Infrastructure and General Government Appropriations Subcommittee of the Legislature that:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(2)(a): includes details on:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(2)(a)(i): the types of fees charged and collected by the Judiciary;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(2)(a)(ii): the methods used to determine the amount of each fee charged and collected by the Judiciary;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(2)(a)(iii): the Judiciary's estimated cost related to each fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(2)(a)(iv): whether each fee is intended to cover the Judiciary's cost related to the fee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(2)(a)(v): the number of fee waivers granted by the Judiciary for each type of fee charged and collected by the Judiciary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(2)(b): include any recommendations regarding fees charged and collected by the Judiciary.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3): (2)(b) If the Judicial Council recommends that the Legislature create a fee or modify an existing fee under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3)(a): the title or purpose of the fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3)(b): the present amount of the fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3)(c): the proposed amount of the fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3)(d): the percent that the fee will have increased or decreased if the Legislature approves the modification of the fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3)(e): the estimated total annual revenue and total estimated annual revenue change that will result from the creation or modification of the fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3)(f): the account or fund into which the fee will be deposited;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3)(g): the reason for the creating or modifying the fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3)(h): the estimated number of persons to be charged the fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3)(i): the Judiciary's estimated cost related to the fee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-310(3)(j): whether the fee is intended to cover the Judiciary's cost related to the fee.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-401 Title.
--------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Court Reporter Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-402 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-402(1): Title 58, Chapter 74, State Certification of Court Reporters Act "Certified court reporter" means a state certified court reporter as described in
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-402(2): "Official court transcriber" means a person certified and authorized in accordance with rules of the Judicial Council to transcribe into written form an audio or video recording of court proceedings.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-403 Appointment of court reporters -- Eligibility.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person may not be appointed to the position of court reporter nor act in the capacity of a court reporter in any court of record of this state, or before any referee, master, board, or commission of this state unless the person is a state certified court reporter in accordance with the provisions of

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-404 Contract restrictions.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-404(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-404(1)(a): Any contract for court reporting services, not related to a particular case or reporting incident, is prohibited between a court reporter or any other person with whom a court reporter has a principal and agency relationship and any attorney, party to an action, or party having a financial interest in an action.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-404(1)(b): Negotiating or bidding reasonable fees, equal to all the parties, on a case-by-case basis is not prohibited.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-404(2): A certified court reporter is an officer of the court, authorized to administer oaths, whose impartiality shall remain beyond question.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-404(3): This section does not apply to the courts or the administrative tribunals of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-404(4): 58-74-102; 58-74-502 Violation of this section shall be considered unprofessional conduct as provided in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-405 Record of court proceedings.
------------------------------------------------------------
The Judicial Council shall by rule provide for the means of maintaining the record of proceedings in the courts of record by official court reporters or by electronic recording devices.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408 Transcripts and copies -- Fees.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(1): The Judicial Council shall by rule provide for a standard page format for transcripts of court proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(a): Except as provided in Subsections (2)(c), (2)(e), and (2)(g), the base rate for a transcript of a court session, or any part of a court session, may not be more than:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(a)(i): $6.00 per page for the body of the transcript, which includes the initial preparation of the transcript and one certified copy; plus
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(a)(ii): $0.50 per page for the word index.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(b): The preparer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(b)(i): deposit the original text file with the clerk of the court by means of an approved electronic filing service provider; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(b)(ii): provide the person requesting the transcript with an electronic certified copy.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(c): The cost of additional copies of the transcript shall be $0.50 per page.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(d): The transcript for an appeal shall be prepared within the time period permitted by the Utah Rules of Appellate Procedure.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(e): The fee for a transcript that is guaranteed to be prepared:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(e)(i): within one business day of the request shall be double the base rate;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(e)(ii): within three business days of the request shall be 1.75 times the base rate;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(e)(iii): within one calendar week shall be 1.5 times the base rate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(e)(iv): within two calendar weeks shall be 1.25 times the base rate.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(f): Payment for a transcript under this section is the responsibility of the party requesting the transcript, except for a court ordered transcript as provided in Subsection (3)(a), and the time for production of the transcript begins once financial arrangements are made with the certified court transcriber.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(2)(g): Child welfare cases shall be billed at the two calendar week rate to meet the deadlines of the Utah Appellate Courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(3): 78B-22-102; 78B-22-203
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(3)(a): When a transcript is ordered by the court, the fees shall be paid by the parties to the action in equal proportion or as ordered by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-408(3)(b): 78B-22-102; 78B-22-203 The fee for a transcript in a criminal case in which the defendant is found to be an indigent individual, as defined in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-409 Certified transcripts prima facie correct.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
A transcript of a certified court reporter's notes, written in longhand or typewritten, certified by the court reporter as being a correct transcript of evidence and proceedings, is prima facie a correct statement of the evidence and proceedings.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-410 Transcripts taxed as costs.
-----------------------------------------------------------
A transcript may not be taxed as costs, unless the preparation of the transcript is ordered either by a party or by the court.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-411 Crimes.
---------------------------------------
Any violation of the provisions of this chapter, except Section

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-602 Court Security Account -- Creation -- Funding -- Uses.
