Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-701 Title.
--------------------------------------
This part is known as the "District Court Guardian ad Litem Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-702 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-702(1): "Attorney guardian ad litem" means an attorney employed by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-702(2): "Director" means the director of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-702(3): "Guardian ad litem" means an attorney guardian ad litem or a private attorney guardian ad litem.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-702(4): 78A-2-802 "Office" means the Office of Guardian ad Litem, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-702(5): 78A-2-705 "Private attorney guardian ad litem" means an attorney designated by the office in accordance with Section

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(1): (1)(b)(i); 78B-22-102 A district court may appoint an attorney guardian ad litem to represent the best interests of a minor in the following district court matters:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(1)(a): protective order proceedings; and

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(1)(b)(iv): the district court determines that there are no private attorney guardians ad litem who are reasonably available to be appointed in the district court action.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(2): (2)(a); (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(2)(a): A court may not appoint an attorney guardian ad litem in a criminal case.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(2)(c)(ii): the interests of the minor may be impacted by:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(2)(c)(ii)(A): an order that has been, or may be, issued in the criminal case; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(2)(c)(ii)(B): other proceedings that have occurred, or may occur, in the criminal case.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(3)(c)(ii): terminating the appointment of the attorney guardian ad litem in the case.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(4): A court shall issue an order terminating the appointment of an attorney guardian ad litem made under this section, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(4)(a): the court determines that the allegations of abuse or neglect are unfounded;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(4)(b): after receiving input from the attorney guardian ad litem, the court determines that the children are no longer at risk of abuse or neglect; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(4)(c): there has been no activity in the case for which the attorney guardian ad litem is appointed for a period of six consecutive months.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(5): (3)(c); (3)(c) A court may issue a written order extending the one-year period described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(6): When appointing an attorney guardian ad litem for a minor under this section, a court may appoint the same attorney guardian ad litem who represents the minor in another proceeding, or who has represented the minor in a previous proceeding, if that attorney guardian ad litem is available.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-703(7): The court is responsible for all costs resulting from the appointment of an attorney guardian ad litem and shall use funds appropriated by the Legislature for the guardian ad litem program to cover those costs.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704 Public policy regarding attorney guardian ad litem -- Training.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(1): An attorney guardian ad litem may not presume that a child and the child's parent are adversaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2): 80-2a-201 An attorney guardian ad litem shall be trained on and implement into practice:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(a): 80-2a-201 the parental rights and child and family protection principles provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(b): the fundamental liberties of parents and the public policy of the state to support family unification to the fullest extent possible;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(c): the constitutionally protected rights of parents, in cases where the state is a party;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(d): the use of a least restrictive means analysis regarding state claims of a compelling child welfare interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(e): the priority of maintaining a child safely in the child's home, whenever possible;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(f): the importance of:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(f)(i): kinship placement, in the event the child is removed from the home; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(f)(ii): keeping sibling groups together, whenever practicable and in the best interests of the children;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(g): the preference for kinship adoption over nonkinship adoption, if the parent-child relationship is legally terminated;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(h): the potential for a guardianship placement if the parent-child relationship is legally terminated and no appropriate adoption placement is available; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(2)(i): the use of an individualized permanency plan, only as a last resort.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-704(3): (2)(e); (i) The office shall implement policies and practice guidelines that reflect the priorities described in Subsections

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(8)(a): (3)(c); (d) Upon receipt of the court's order, described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(8)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(8)(b)(i): If, after the initial assignment of a private attorney guardian ad litem, either party objects to the assigned private attorney guardian ad litem, that party may file an objection with the court within seven days after the day on which the party received notice of the assigned private attorney guardian ad litem.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(8)(b)(ii): If, after the initial assignment of a private attorney guardian ad litem, either attorney for a party discovers that the private attorney guardian ad litem represents an adverse party in a separate matter, that attorney may file an objection with the court within seven days after the day on which the attorney received notice of the private attorney guardian ad litem's representation of an adverse party in a separate matter.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(8)(b)(iii): Upon receipt of an objection, the court shall determine whether grounds exist for the objection, and if grounds exist, the court shall order, without a hearing, the office to assign a new private attorney guardian ad litem, in consultation with the parties and in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(8)(b)(iv): If no alternative private attorney guardian ad litem is available, the office shall notify the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(9): (17); 78A-2-302
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(9)(a): (17) When appointing a private attorney guardian ad litem, the court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(9)(a)(i): assess all or part of the private attorney guardian ad litem fees, court costs, and paralegal, staff, and volunteer expenses against the parties in a proportion the court determines to be just; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(9)(a)(ii): (17) designate in the order whether the private attorney guardian ad litem shall, as established by rule under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(9)(a)(ii)(A): be paid a set fee and initial retainer;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(9)(a)(ii)(B): not be paid and serve pro bono; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(9)(a)(ii)(C): be paid at a rate less than the set fee established by court rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(9)(b): 78A-2-302 If a party claims to be indigent, the court shall follow the procedure and make a determination, as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(9)(c): The private attorney guardian ad litem may adjust the court-ordered fees or retainer to an amount less than what was ordered by the court at any time before being released from representation by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(10): Upon accepting the court's appointment, the assigned private attorney guardian ad litem shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(10)(a): file a notice of appearance with the court within five business days of the day on which the attorney was assigned; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(10)(b): represent the best interests of the minor until released by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(11): The private attorney guardian ad litem:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(11)(a): shall be certified by the director of the office as meeting the minimum qualifications for appointment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(11)(b): may not be employed by, or under contract with, the office unless under contract as a conflict private attorney guardian ad litem in an unrelated case.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12): The private attorney guardian ad litem appointed under the provisions of this section shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(a): represent the best interests of the minor from the date of the appointment until released by the court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(b): conduct or supervise an ongoing, independent investigation in order to obtain, first-hand, a clear understanding of the situation and needs of the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(c): interview witnesses and review relevant records pertaining to the minor and the minor's family, including medical, psychological, and school records;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(i): personally meet with the minor, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(i)(A): the minor is outside of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(i)(B): meeting with the minor would be detrimental to the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(ii): personally interview the minor, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(ii)(A): the minor is not old enough to communicate;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(ii)(B): the minor lacks the capacity to participate in a meaningful interview; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(ii)(C): the interview would be detrimental to the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(iii): to the extent possible, determine the minor's goals and concerns regarding custody or visitation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(iv): to the extent possible, and unless it would be detrimental to the minor, keep the minor advised of:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(iv)(A): the status of the minor's case;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(iv)(B): all court and administrative proceedings;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(iv)(C): discussions with, and proposals made by, other parties;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(iv)(D): court action; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(d)(iv)(E): the psychiatric, medical, or other treatment or diagnostic services that are to be provided to the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(e): unless excused by the court, prepare for and attend all mediation hearings and all court conferences and hearings, and present witnesses and exhibits as necessary to protect the best interests of the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(f): identify community resources to protect the best interests of the minor and advocate for those resources; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(12)(g): participate in all appeals unless excused by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(13): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(13)(a): The private attorney guardian ad litem shall represent the best interests of a minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(13)(b): If the minor's intent and desires differ from the private attorney guardian ad litem's determination of the minor's best interests, the private attorney guardian ad litem shall communicate to the court the minor's intent and desires and the private attorney guardian ad litem's determination of the minor's best interests.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(13)(c): A difference between the minor's intent and desires and the private attorney guardian ad litem's determination of best interests is not sufficient to create a conflict of interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(13)(d): The private attorney guardian ad litem shall disclose the intent and desires of the minor unless the minor:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(13)(d)(i): instructs the private attorney guardian ad litem to not disclose the minor's intent and desires; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(13)(d)(ii): has not expressed an intent and desire.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(13)(e): The court may appoint one private attorney guardian ad litem to represent the best interests of more than one child of a marriage.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(14): In every court hearing where the private attorney guardian ad litem makes a recommendation regarding the best interest of the minor, the court shall require the private attorney guardian ad litem to disclose the factors that form the basis of the recommendation.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(15): A private attorney guardian ad litem appointed under this section is immune from any civil liability that might result by reason of acts performed within the scope of duties of the private attorney guardian ad litem.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(16): The office and the Guardian ad Litem Oversight Committee shall compile a list of attorneys willing to accept an appointment as a private attorney guardian ad litem.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(17): Upon the advice of the director and the Guardian ad Litem Oversight Committee, the Judicial Council shall establish by rule:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(17)(a): the minimum qualifications and requirements for appointment by the court as a private attorney guardian ad litem;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(17)(b): the standard fee rate and retainer amount for a private attorney guardian ad litem;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(17)(c): the percentage of cases a private attorney guardian ad litem may be expected to take on pro bono;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(17)(d): a system to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(17)(d)(i): select a private attorney guardian ad litem for a given appointment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(17)(d)(ii): determine when a private attorney guardian ad litem shall be expected to accept an appointment pro bono; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(17)(e): the process for handling a complaint relating to the eligibility status of a private attorney guardian ad litem.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(18): (18)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-705(18)(a): Any savings that result from assigning a private attorney guardian ad litem in a district court case, instead of an office guardian ad litem, shall be applied to the office to recruit and train attorneys for the private attorney guardian ad litem program.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(d)(i): personally meets with the minor, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(d)(i)(A): the minor is outside of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(d)(i)(B): meeting with the minor would be detrimental to the minor;

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(d)(ii)(A): the minor is not old enough to communicate;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(d)(ii)(B): the minor lacks the capacity to participate in a meaningful interview; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(d)(ii)(C): the interview would be detrimental to the minor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(d)(iii): if the minor is placed in an out-of-home placement, or is being considered for placement in an out-of-home placement, unless it would be detrimental to the minor:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(d)(iii)(A): to the extent possible, determines the minor's goals and concerns regarding placement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(d)(iii)(B): personally assesses or supervises an assessment of the appropriateness and safety of the minor's environment in each placement;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(e): personally attends all review hearings pertaining to the minor's case;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(f): participates in all appeals, unless excused by order of the court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(g): is familiar with local experts who can provide consultation and testimony regarding the reasonableness and appropriateness of efforts made by the division to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(g)(i): maintain a minor in the minor's home; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(g)(ii): reunify a minor with a minor's parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(h): to the extent possible, and unless it would be detrimental to the minor, personally or through a trained volunteer, paralegal, or other trained staff, keeps the minor advised of:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(h)(i): the status of the minor's case;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(h)(ii): all court and administrative proceedings;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(h)(iii): discussions with, and proposals made by, other parties;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(h)(iv): court action; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(h)(v): the psychiatric, medical, or other treatment or diagnostic services that are to be provided to the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(i): in cases where a child and family plan is required, personally or through a trained volunteer, paralegal, or other trained staff, monitors implementation of a minor's child and family plan and any dispositional orders to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(i)(i): determine whether services ordered by the court:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(i)(i)(A): are actually provided; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(i)(i)(B): are provided in a timely manner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(i)(ii): attempt to assess whether services ordered by the court are accomplishing the intended goal of the services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-2-803(3)(j): makes all necessary court filings to advance the guardian's ad litem position regarding the best interest of the minor.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Chapter 3 - Supreme Court
***********************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101 Number of justices -- Terms -- Chief justice and associate chief justice -- Selection and functions.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(1): The Supreme Court consists of five justices.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(2)(a): A justice of the Supreme Court shall be appointed initially to serve until the first general election held more than three years after the effective date of the appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(2)(b): (2)(a) After the first term of appointment under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(2)(c): A justice whose term expires may serve upon request of the Judicial Council until a successor is appointed and qualified.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(3)(a): The justices of the Supreme Court shall elect a chief justice from among the members of the court by a majority vote of all justices.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(3)(b): The term of the office of chief justice is four years.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(3)(c): The chief justice may serve successive terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(3)(d): The chief justice may resign from the office of chief justice without resigning from the Supreme Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(3)(e): The chief justice may be removed from the office of chief justice by a majority vote of all justices of the Supreme Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(3)(f): The chief justice shall receive the sum of $2,000 per annum as additional compensation for the period served as chief justice.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(4)(a): If the justices are unable to elect a chief justice within 30 days of a vacancy in that office, the associate chief justice shall act as chief justice until a chief justice is elected under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(4)(b): If the associate chief justice is unable or unwilling to act as chief justice, the most senior justice shall act as chief justice until a chief justice is elected under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(5): In addition to the chief justice's duties as a member of the Supreme Court, the chief justice has duties as provided by law.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(6)(a): There is created the office of associate chief justice.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(6)(b): The term of office of the associate chief justice is two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(6)(c): The associate chief justice shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(6)(c)(i): elected by a majority vote of the members of the Supreme Court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(6)(c)(ii): allocated duties as the chief justice determines.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(6)(d): If the chief justice is absent or otherwise unable to serve, the associate chief justice shall serve as chief justice.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(6)(e): The chief justice may delegate responsibilities to the associate chief justice as consistent with law.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-101(6)(f): The associate chief justice shall receive the sum of $1,000 per annum for the period served as associate chief justice.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102 Supreme Court jurisdiction.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(1): The Supreme Court has original jurisdiction to answer questions of state law certified by a court of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(2): The Supreme Court has original jurisdiction to issue all extraordinary writs and authority to issue all writs and process necessary to carry into effect its orders, judgments, and decrees or in aid of its jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3): (3)(e) The Supreme Court has appellate jurisdiction, including jurisdiction of interlocutory appeals, over:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(a): a judgment of the Court of Appeals;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(b): cases certified to the Supreme Court by the Court of Appeals prior to final judgment by the Court of Appeals;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(c): discipline of lawyers;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(d): final orders of the Judicial Conduct Commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(e): final orders and decrees in formal adjudicative proceedings originating with:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(e)(i): the Public Service Commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(e)(ii): the State Tax Commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(e)(iii): the School and Institutional Trust Lands Board of Trustees;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(e)(iv): the Board of Oil, Gas, and Mining;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(e)(v): the state engineer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(e)(vi): the executive director of the Department of Natural Resources reviewing actions of the Division of Forestry, Fire, and State Lands;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(f): (3)(e) final orders and decrees of the district court review of informal adjudicative proceedings of agencies under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(g): a final judgment or decree of any court of record holding a statute of the United States or this state unconstitutional on its face under the Constitution of the United States or the Utah Constitution;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(h): interlocutory appeals from any court of record involving a charge of a first degree or capital felony;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(i): appeals from the district court involving a conviction or charge of a first degree felony or capital felony;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(j): orders, judgments, and decrees of any court of record over which the Court of Appeals does not have original appellate jurisdiction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(3)(k): appeals from the district court of orders, judgments, or decrees ruling on legislative subpoenas.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(4): (3)(a); (d) The Supreme Court may transfer to the Court of Appeals any of the matters over which the Supreme Court has original appellate jurisdiction, except:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(4)(a): capital felony convictions or an appeal of an interlocutory order of a court of record involving a charge of a capital felony;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(4)(b): election and voting contests;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(4)(c): reapportionment of election districts;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(4)(d): retention or removal of public officers;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(4)(e): matters involving legislative subpoenas; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(4)(f): (3)(a); (d) those matters described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(5): (3)(b) The Supreme Court has sole discretion in granting or denying a petition for writ of certiorari for the review of a Court of Appeals adjudication, but the Supreme Court shall review those cases certified to it by the Court of Appeals under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-102(6): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act The Supreme Court shall comply with the requirements of


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-103 Supreme Court -- Rulemaking, judges pro tempore, and practice of law.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-103(1): The Supreme Court shall adopt rules of procedure and evidence for use in the courts of the state and shall by rule manage the appellate process.  The Legislature may amend the rules of procedure and evidence adopted by the Supreme Court upon a vote of two-thirds of all members of both houses of the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-103(2): Except as otherwise provided by the Utah Constitution, the Supreme Court by rule may authorize retired justices and judges and judges pro tempore to perform any judicial duties.  Judges pro tempore shall be citizens of the United States, Utah residents, and admitted to practice law in Utah.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-103(3): The Supreme Court shall by rule govern the practice of law, including admission to practice law and the conduct and discipline of persons admitted to the practice of law.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-104 Appellate court administrator.
--------------------------------------------------------------
The appellate court administrator shall appoint clerks and support staff as necessary for the operation of the Supreme Court and the Court of Appeals.  The duties of the clerks and support staff shall be established by the appellate court administrator, and powers established by rule of the Supreme Court.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-3-105 Service of sheriff to court.
------------------------------------------------------------
The court may at any time require the attendance and services of any sheriff in the state.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Chapter 4 - Court of Appeals
**************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-101 Creation -- Seal.
-------------------------------------------------
There is created a court known as the Court of Appeals.  The Court of Appeals is a court of record and shall have a seal.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102 Number of judges -- Terms -- Presiding judge -- Associate presiding judge -- Filing fees.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(1): (1)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(1)(a): The Court of Appeals consists of seven judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(1)(b): The term of appointment to office as a judge of the Court of Appeals is until the first general election held more than three years after the effective date of the appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(1)(c): (1)(b) After the first term of appointment under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(1)(d): A judge whose term expires may serve, upon request of the Judicial Council, until a successor is appointed and qualified.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(2)(a): The Court of Appeals shall sit and render judgment in panels of three judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(2)(b): Assignment to panels shall be by random rotation of all judges of the Court of Appeals.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(2)(c): The Court of Appeals by rule shall provide for the selection of a chair for each panel.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(2)(d): The Court of Appeals may not sit en banc.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(3)(a): The judges of the Court of Appeals shall elect a presiding judge from among the members of the court by majority vote of all judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(3)(b): The term of office of the presiding judge is two years and until a successor is elected.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(3)(c): A presiding judge of the Court of Appeals may serve in that office no more than two successive terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(3)(d): The Court of Appeals may by rule provide for an acting presiding judge to serve in the absence or incapacity of the presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(3)(e): The presiding judge of the Court of Appeals shall receive $2,000 per annum of additional compensation for the period served as presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(4)(a): The presiding judge may be removed from the office of presiding judge by majority vote of all judges of the Court of Appeals.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(4)(b): In addition to the duties of a judge of the Court of Appeals, the presiding judge shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(4)(b)(i): administer the rotation and scheduling of panels;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(4)(b)(ii): act as liaison with the Supreme Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(4)(b)(iii): call and preside over the meetings of the Court of Appeals; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(4)(b)(iv): carry out duties prescribed by the Supreme Court and the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(5)(a): The judges of the Court of Appeals shall elect an associate presiding judge from among the members of the court by majority vote of all judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(5)(b): The associate presiding judge of the Court of Appeals shall receive $1,000 per annum as additional compensation for the period served as associate presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-102(6): Filing fees for the Court of Appeals are the same as for the Supreme Court.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-103 Court of Appeals jurisdiction.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-103(1): Title 63G, Chapter 2, Part 4, Appeals; 63G-2-404 As used in this section, "adjudicative proceeding" does not include a proceeding under

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-103(2)(b): in aid of its jurisdiction.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-103(3)(a): 19-1-301.5; 53G-11-515

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-104 Location of Court of Appeals.
-------------------------------------------------------------
The Court of Appeals has its principal location in Salt Lake City.  The Court of Appeals may perform any of its functions in any location within the state.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-105 Review of actions by Supreme Court.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Review of the judgments, orders, and decrees of the Court of Appeals shall be by petition for writ of certiorari to the Supreme Court.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-106(3): The Chief Appellate Mediator may disclose statistical and other demographic information as may be necessary and useful to report on the status and to allow supervision and oversight of the Appellate Mediation Office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-106(4): Title 63G, Chapter 7, Governmental Immunity Act of Utah When acting as mediators, the Chief Appellate Mediator and other professional staff of the Appellate Mediation Office shall be immune from liability pursuant to
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-106(5): Pursuant to


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-4-201 Appellate review of juvenile courts.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
To uphold the clear and compelling fundamental liberty interests and constitutionally protected rights of parents and the strong public policy in favor of maximizing family unification, appropriate appellate review shall be made available and applied in furtherance of those interests.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-101 State District Court Administrative System -- Definitions.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-101(1): 76-1-401 As used in this chapter:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-101(1)(a): "Court system" means the State District Court Administrative System.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-101(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-101(2)(a): The district court is a trial court of general jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-101(2)(b): A district court shall be located in the county seat of each county.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-101(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-101(3)(a): There is established a State District Court Administrative System.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-101(3)(b): The Judicial Council shall administer the operation of the court system.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-103 District court case management.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-103(1): The district court of each district shall develop systems of case management.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-103(2): The case management systems developed by a district court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-103(2)(a): ensure judicial accountability for the just and timely disposition of cases; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-103(2)(b): provide for each judge a full judicial work load that accommodates differences in the subject matter or complexity of cases assigned to different judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-103(3): A district court may establish divisions within the court for the efficient management of different types of cases.  The existence of divisions within the court may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-103(3)(a): affect the jurisdiction of the court nor the validity of court orders; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-103(3)(b): impede public access to the courts.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-104 Terms -- Minimum of once quarterly.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Each district court shall hold court at the county seat of each county within the district at least once in each quarter of the year.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-105 Term of judges -- Vacancy.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-105(1): Judges of the district courts shall be appointed initially until the first general election held more than three years after the effective date of the appointment.  Thereafter, the term of office for judges of the district courts is six years, and commences on the first Monday in January, next following the date of election.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-105(2): A judge whose term expires may serve, upon request of the Judicial Council, until a successor is appointed and qualified.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106 Presiding judge -- Associate presiding judge -- Election -- Term -- Compensation -- Powers -- Duties.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106(1): In judicial districts having more than one district court judge, the district court judges shall elect one judge of the district to the office of presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106(2): In judicial districts having more than two district court judges, the district court judges may elect one judge of the district to the office of associate presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106(3): The presiding judge shall receive an additional $2,000 per annum as compensation for the period served as presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106(4): The associate presiding judge shall receive an additional $1,000 per annum as compensation for the period served as associate presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106(5): The presiding judge has the following authority and responsibilities, consistent with the policies of the Judicial Council:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106(5)(a): implementing policies of the Judicial Council; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106(5)(b): exercising powers and performing administrative duties as authorized by the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106(6)(a): When the presiding judge is unavailable, the associate presiding judge shall assume the responsibilities of the presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-106(6)(b): The associate presiding judge shall perform other duties assigned by the presiding judge.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107 Court commissioners -- Qualifications -- Appointment -- Functions governed by rule.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(1): 78A-2-221
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(1)(a): Court commissioners are quasi-judicial officers of courts of record and have limited judicial authority as provided by this section and rules of the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(1)(b): 78A-2-221 Court commissioners serve full-time and are subject to the restrictions of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(2)(a): The Judicial Council shall appoint court commissioners with the concurrence of a majority of the judges of trial courts in the district the court commissioner primarily serves.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(2)(b): The Judicial Council may assign court commissioners appointed under this section to serve in one or more judicial districts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(3): A person appointed as a court commissioner shall have the following qualifications:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(3)(a): be 25 years old or older;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(3)(b): be a citizen of the United States;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(3)(c): be a resident of this state while serving as court commissioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(3)(d): be admitted to the practice of law in this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(3)(e): possess ability and experience in the areas of law in which the commissioner will be serving.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(4): A court commissioner shall take and subscribe to the oath of office as required by Article IV, Sec. 10, Utah Constitution, prior to assuming the duties of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(5): Court commissioners shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(5)(a): comply with applicable constitutional and statutory provisions, court rules and procedures, and rules of the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(5)(b): comply with the Code of Judicial Conduct to the same extent as full-time judges; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(5)(c): successfully complete orientation and education programs as required by the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(6): The presiding judge of the district the commissioner primarily serves:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(6)(a): shall develop a performance plan for the court commissioner and annually conduct an evaluation of the commissioner's performance, and shall provide the plan and evaluations to the Judicial Council upon request; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(6)(b): is responsible for the day-to-day supervision of the court commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(7): 78A-2-104(6) The Judicial Council shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(7)(a): establish by rule procedures for the investigation and review of complaints and the discipline and removal of court commissioners; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(7)(b): 78A-2-104(6) evaluate court commissioners under the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(8): The Judicial Council shall make uniform statewide rules defining the duties and authority of court commissioners for each level of court they serve.  The rules shall not exceed constitutional limitations upon the delegation of judicial authority.  The rules shall at a minimum establish:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(8)(a): types of cases and matters commissioners may hear;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(8)(b): types of orders commissioners may recommend;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(8)(c): types of relief commissioners may recommend; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-107(8)(d): procedure for timely judicial review of recommendations and orders made by court commissioners.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-108 Duties of the clerk of the district court.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
The clerk of the district court shall:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-108(1): take charge of and safely keep the court seal;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-108(2): take charge of and safely keep or dispose of all books, papers, and records filed or deposited with the clerk, and all other records required by law or the rules of the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-108(3): issue all notices, processes, and summonses as authorized by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-108(4): keep a record of all proceedings, actions, orders, judgments, and decrees of the court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-108(5): take and certify acknowledgments and administer oaths;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-108(6): supervise the deputy clerks as required to perform the duties of the clerk's office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-108(7): perform other duties as required by the presiding judge, the court executive, applicable law, and the rules of the Judicial Council.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111 Transfer of court operating responsibilities -- Facilities -- Staff -- Budget.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(1): A county's determination to transfer responsibility for operation of the district court to the state is irrevocable.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(2)(a): Court space suitable for the conduct of judicial business as specified by the Judicial Council shall be provided by the state from appropriations made by the Legislature for these purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(2)(b): The state may, in order to carry out its obligation to provide these facilities, lease space from a county, or reimburse a county for the number of square feet used by the district.  Any lease and reimbursement shall be determined in accordance with the standards of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management applicable to state agencies generally.  A county or municipality terminating a lease with the court shall provide written notice to the Judicial Council at least one year prior to the effective date of the termination.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(2)(c): District courts shall be located in municipalities that are sites for the district court or circuit court as of January 1, 1994.  Removal of the district court from the municipality shall require prior legislative approval by joint resolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(3): The state shall provide legal reference materials for all district judges' chambers and courtrooms, as required by Judicial Council rule.  Maintenance of county law libraries shall be in consultation with the court executive of the district court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(4): (4)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(4)(a): At the request of the Judicial Council, the county or municipality shall provide staff for the district court in county seats or municipalities under contract with the administrative office of the courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(4)(b): Payment for necessary expenses shall be by a contract entered into annually between the state and the county or municipality, which shall specifically state the agreed costs of personnel, supplies, and services, as well as the method and terms of payment.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(4)(c): Workload measures prepared by the state court administrator and projected costs for the next fiscal year shall be considered in the negotiation of contracts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-111(4)(d): (4)(b) Each May 1 preceding the general session of the Legislature, the county or municipality shall submit a budget request to the Judicial Council, the governor, and the legislative fiscal analyst for services to be rendered as part of the contract under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201 Creation and expansion of existing drug court programs -- Definition of drug court program -- Criteria for participation in drug court programs -- Reporting requirements.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(1): There may be created a drug court program in any judicial district that demonstrates:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(1)(a): the need for a drug court program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(1)(b): the existence of a collaborative strategy between the court, prosecutors, defense counsel, corrections, and substance abuse treatment services to reduce substance abuse by offenders.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(2): The collaborative strategy in each drug court program shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(2)(a): include monitoring and evaluation components to measure program effectiveness; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(2)(b): be submitted to, for the purpose of coordinating the disbursement of funding, the:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(2)(b)(i): executive director of the Department of Health and Human Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(2)(b)(ii): executive director of the Department of Corrections; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(2)(b)(iii): state court administrator.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(3)(a): Funds disbursed to a drug court program shall be allocated as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(3)(a)(i): 87% to the Department of Health and Human Services for testing, treatment, and case management; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(3)(a)(ii): 13% to the Administrative Office of the Courts for increased judicial and court support costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(3)(b): This provision does not apply to federal block grant funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(4): A drug court program shall include continuous judicial supervision using a cooperative approach with prosecutors, defense counsel, corrections, substance abuse treatment services, juvenile court probation, and the Division of Child and Family Services as appropriate to promote public safety, protect participants' due process rights, and integrate substance abuse treatment with justice system case processing.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(5): Screening criteria for participation in a drug court program shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(5)(a): a plea to, conviction of, or adjudication for a nonviolent drug offense or drug-related offense;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(5)(b): an agreement to frequent alcohol and other drug testing;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(5)(c): participation in one or more substance abuse treatment programs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(5)(d): an agreement to submit to sanctions for noncompliance with drug court program requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(6): 58-37-8
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(6)(a): The Judicial Council shall develop rules prescribing eligibility requirements for participation in adult criminal drug courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(6)(b): 58-37-8 The eligibility requirements described in Subsection (6)(a):
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(6)(b)(i): shall require that the acceptance of an offender into a drug court is based on a risk and needs assessment and targeted at individuals who are high risk and high needs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(6)(b)(ii): 58-37-8 may not limit participation in a drug court only to individuals convicted of an offense described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-201(6)(c): A plea to, conviction of, or adjudication for a felony offense is not required for participation in a drug court program.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-202 Creation of Drug Board Pilot Project -- Definition of Drug Board Pilot Project -- Criteria for parolee participation in the Drug Board Pilot Project -- Reporting requirements.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-202(1): There may be created a Drug Board Pilot Project in Davis and Weber counties that includes intensive substance abuse treatment, frequent drug testing, and other additional conditions of parole, with the expectation that the offender will be required to complete the substance abuse treatment, remain drug free, and meet all other conditions of parole.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-202(2): Screening criteria for parolee participation in the Drug Board Pilot Project shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-202(2)(a): be determined by the Board of Pardons and Parole and the Department of Corrections; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-202(2)(b): include parolees who are facing an eminent return to prison due to substance abuse.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-301.5 Title.
----------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Veterans Treatment Court Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(1): "Defendant" means a veteran charged with a criminal offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(2): 77-36-1 "Domestic violence" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(3): 78A-5-304(1); 78A-5-310
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(3)(a): 78A-5-304(1) "Participant agreement" means the record, required by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(3)(b): 78A-5-310 "Participant agreement" includes a modification under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(4): 78A-5-307(1)(c) "Record," except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(5): 68-3-12.5 " Service member" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(5)(a): 68-3-12.5 a member of the active or reserve components of the armed forces as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(5)(b): a member of the National Guard of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(6)(a): "State" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, or any territory or insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(6)(b): "State" includes a federally recognized Indian tribe.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(7): "Veteran" means a former service member who qualifies for health care benefits from the Veterans Administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-302(8): "Veterans treatment court" means a veterans treatment court program administered under this part by a court of this state.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303 Creation of a veterans treatment court.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(1): The Judicial Council may create a veterans treatment court in any judicial district or geographic region that demonstrates:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(1)(a): the need for a veterans treatment court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(1)(b): the existence of a collaborative strategy between the veterans treatment court, prosecutors, defense attorneys, substance abuse treatment services, the Department of Corrections, and the United States Department of Veterans Affairs Veterans Justice Outreach Program to work with veteran offenders.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(2): A veterans treatment court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(2)(a): establish a collaborative strategy that includes monitoring and evaluation components to measure program effectiveness; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(2)(b): submit a collaborative strategy, for the purpose of coordinating the disbursement of funding, to the Administrative Office of the Courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(3): A veterans treatment court shall include continuous judicial supervision using a cooperative approach with prosecutors, defense attorneys, substance abuse treatment services, the Department of Corrections, and the United States Department of Veterans Affairs Veterans Justice Outreach Program, as appropriate, to promote public safety, protect participants' due process rights, and integrate veteran treatment programs with the justice system case processing.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(4): Screening criteria for participation in a veterans treatment court shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(4)(a): a plea in abeyance or plea agreement for a criminal offense, or a requirement for participation in a veterans treatment court as a condition of probation;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(4)(b): frequent alcohol and other drug testing, if appropriate;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(4)(c): participation in veteran outreach programs, including substance abuse treatment programs where appropriate;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(4)(d): sanctions for noncompliance with the requirements for participation in a veterans treatment court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(4)(e): any additional criteria developed by a veterans treatment court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(5): No later than October 1 each year, the Administrative Office of the Courts shall provide to the Executive Offices and Criminal Justice Appropriations Subcommittee a written report describing:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(5)(a): the types of policies and procedures adopted by veteran treatment courts;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(5)(b): the number of veteran participants in the previous fiscal year;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(5)(c): the outcomes for veteran participants in the previous fiscal year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-303(5)(d): recommendations for future veterans treatment courts, including expansion and funding.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-304 Record of policies and procedures.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-304(1): 78A-5-305; 78A-5-312 A veterans treatment court shall create a record of policies and procedures adopted to implement Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-304(2): 78A-5-305; 78A-5-312 A veterans treatment court shall seek input from prosecutors, defense attorneys, and other interested persons in developing and adopting policies and procedures to implement Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305 Policies and procedures for a veterans treatment court.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1): A veterans treatment court shall adopt policies and procedures to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1)(a): integrate alcohol-treatment, drug-treatment, and mental-health services with the defendant's criminal case;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1)(b): use a nonadversarial approach in which prosecutors and defense attorneys promote public safety while protecting due-process rights of defendants;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1)(c): exercise early identification of eligible defendants;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1)(d): provide access to a continuum of alcohol-treatment, drug-treatment, mental-health treatment, and other related treatment and rehabilitation services;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1)(e): monitor defendants for abstinence from alcohol and drugs by frequent testing;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1)(f): direct a coordinated strategy that responds to each defendant's needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1)(g): provide ongoing judicial interaction with each defendant;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1)(h): monitor and evaluate the achievement of goals;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1)(i): continue interdisciplinary education to promote effective veterans treatment court planning, implementation, and operations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(1)(j): forge partnerships between the veterans treatment court and the United States Department of Veterans Affairs Veterans Justice Outreach Program, the Department of Veterans and Military Affairs, public agencies, and community-based organizations to generate local support and enhance the effectiveness of the veterans treatment court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-305(2): (1) In adopting policies and procedures under this section, the court shall consider nationally recognized best practices to implement the policies and procedures described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306 Supplemental policies and procedures of veterans treatment court.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306(1): A veterans treatment court may adopt supplemental policies and procedures to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306(1)(a): refer a defendant with a medical or medication need to an appropriate health care provider;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306(1)(b): refer a defendant to other available services, including assistance with housing, employment, nutrition, and education;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306(1)(c): provide a defendant access to a mentor who is a veteran;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306(1)(d): integrate intervention, treatment, and counseling, as part of the rehabilitative services offered to a defendant who has been a victim of domestic violence, sexual trauma, child abuse, or other trauma;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306(1)(e): confer with the victim or alleged victim of the domestic violence offense for which the defendant is charged that serves as the basis for the defendant's participation in the veterans treatment court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306(1)(f): evaluate and assess a defendant charged with a domestic violence offense and integrate specific counseling as part of the total rehabilitative services for the defendant;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306(1)(g): monitor a defendant charged with a domestic violence offense to assure compliance with a domestic violence protection order, no-contact order, and prohibition of weapon possession; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306(1)(h): otherwise assist the veterans treatment court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-306(2): (1) In adopting policies and procedures under this section, the veterans treatment court shall consider nationally recognized best practices related to policies and procedures described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307 Eligibility.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(1): A defendant is eligible to be screened for participation in a veterans treatment court if:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(1)(a): the defendant is a veteran;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(1)(b): the defendant has a mental-health condition, traumatic brain injury, or substance use disorder;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(1)(c): the defendant agrees on the court record to voluntarily:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(1)(c)(i): participate in the veterans treatment court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(1)(c)(ii): enter into a plea in abeyance or plea agreement, or participate in a veterans treatment court as a condition of probation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(1)(c)(iii): adhere to a participant agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(1)(d): as determined by the court, the defendant's participation in the veterans treatment court would be in the interest of justice and of benefit to the defendant and the community.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2): (1)(d) In making the determination under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2)(a): the nature and circumstances of the offense charged;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2)(b): special characteristics or circumstances of the defendant, including the defendant's criminogenic risk and need;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2)(c): the defendant's criminal history and whether the defendant previously participated in a veterans treatment court or a similar program;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2)(d): whether the defendant's needs exceed treatment resources available to the veterans treatment court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2)(e): the impact on the community of the defendant's participation and treatment in the veterans treatment court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2)(f): special characteristics or circumstances of the victim or alleged victim;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2)(g): provision for, and the likelihood of obtaining, restitution from the defendant over the course of participation in the veterans treatment court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2)(h): the recommendation of the prosecutor regarding whether the defendant should participate in a veterans treatment court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2)(i): mitigating circumstances; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(2)(j): other circumstances reasonably related to the defendant, the defendant's case, and available resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-307(3): 77-37-3; (1); (2) Section


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-308 Requirement for admission.
----------------------------------------------------------
For a defendant to be admitted to a veterans treatment court, the defendant and prosecutor must sign, and the court must approve, a participant agreement and a plea in abeyance, plea agreement, or probation agreement.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-309 Victim of domestic violence.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-309(1): If a victim or alleged victim of a domestic violence offense that serves as the basis for the defendant's participation in a veterans treatment court can be reasonably located, the victim or alleged victim must be offered:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-309(1)(a): referrals to domestic violence service providers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-309(1)(b): information on how to report an allegation of:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-309(1)(b)(i): an offense committed by the defendant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-309(1)(b)(ii): a violation by the defendant of the participant agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-309(2): Except as expressly provided for in this part, the participation of the defendant in a veterans treatment court does not alter the rights of a victim or alleged victim of domestic violence under the law of this state.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-310 Modification or termination.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-310(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-310(1)(a): If a prosecutor finds that a defendant has failed to comply with the defendant's participant agreement, the prosecutor may notify the veterans treatment court and the defendant of the defendant's failure to comply with the participant agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-310(1)(b): (1)(a) Any notice by a prosecutor under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-310(2): (1) Upon notice under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-310(3): (2) At the hearing described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-310(3)(a): review the defendant's conduct under the participant agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-310(3)(b): hear recommendations from all parties in order to determine whether the defendant's participation in the veterans treatment court should be modified or terminated.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-310(4): After notice and a hearing is provided in accordance with this section, the veterans treatment court may modify or terminate a defendant's participation in a veterans treatment court.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-311 Completion of the participant agreement.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
If the veterans treatment court determines that a defendant has completed the requirements of the defendant's participant agreement, the court shall adjudicate the defendant's case in accordance with the defendant's participant agreement and any applicable plea in abeyance agreement, plea agreement, probation agreement, court order, or judgment.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-312 No right to participate.
--------------------------------------------------------
This part does not create a right to participation in a veterans treatment court.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5-313 Severability.
---------------------------------------------
If any provision of this part, or the application of any provision of this part to any person or circumstance, is held invalid, the remainder of this part shall be given effect without the invalid provision or application.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Chapter 5a - Business and Chancery Court
**************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(1): "Action" means a lawsuit or case commenced in a court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(2)(a): "Asset" means property of all kinds, real or personal and tangible or intangible.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(2)(b): "Asset" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(2)(b)(i): cash, except for any reasonable compensation or salary for services rendered;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(2)(b)(ii): stock or other investments;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(2)(b)(iii): goodwill;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(2)(b)(iv): an ownership interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(2)(b)(v): a license;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(2)(b)(vi): a cause of action; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(2)(b)(vii): any similar property.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(3): 16-10a-1301 "Beneficial shareholder" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(4): 63A-16-108 "Blockchain" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(5): "Blockchain technology" means computer software or hardware or collections of computer software or hardware, or both, that utilize or enable a blockchain.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(6): "Board" means the board of directors or trustees of a corporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(7): "Business" means any enterprise carried on for the purpose of gain or economic profit.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8): 63G-7-102
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(a): "Business organization" means an organization in any form that is primarily engaged in business.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(b): "Business organization" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(b)(i): an association;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(b)(ii): a corporation;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(b)(iii): a joint stock company;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(b)(iv): a joint venture;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(b)(v): a limited liability company;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(b)(vi): a mutual fund trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(b)(vii): a partnership; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(b)(viii): any other similar form of an organization described in Subsections (8)(b)(i) through (vii).
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(8)(c): 63G-7-102 "Business organization" does not include a governmental entity as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(9): "Claim" means a written demand or assertion in an action.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(10): 78B-6-801 "Commercial tenant" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(11): "Consumer contract" means a contract entered into by a consumer for the purchase of goods or services for personal, family, or household purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(12): 78A-5a-102 "Court" means the Business and Chancery Court established in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(13): 48-5-101 "Decentralized autonomous organization" means the same as that term is defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(15): "Franchisor" means the same as that term is defined in 16 C.F.R. Sec. 436.1.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(16): 63G-7-102 "Governmental entity" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(17): 78B-3-403 "Health care" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(18): 78B-3-403 "Health care provider" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(19): "Monetary damages" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(19)(a): punitive or exemplary damages;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(19)(b): prejudgment or postjudgment interest; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(19)(c): attorney fees or costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(20): "Officer" means an individual designated by a board, or other governing body of a business organization, to act on behalf of the business organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(21): "Owner" means a person who, directly or indirectly, owns or controls an ownership interest in a business organization regardless of whether the person owns or controls the ownership interest through another person, a power of attorney, or another business organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(22): "Ownership interest" means an interest owned in a business organization, including any shares, membership interest, partnership interest, or governance or transferable interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(23): "Personal injury" means a physical or mental injury, including wrongful death.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(24): "Professional" means an individual whose profession requires a license, registration, or certification on the basis of experience, education, testing, or training.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(25):

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(25)(b): "Provisional remedy" includes a preliminary injunction, a temporary restraining order, a prejudgment writ, or an appointment of a receiver.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(26): 61-1-13 "Security" means the same as that term is defined in Section
