Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-101(29): "Trustee" means a person that holds or administers an ownership interest on behalf of a third party.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-102 Establishment of the Business and Chancery Court -- Organization and status.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-102(1): There is established the Business and Chancery Court for the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-102(2): The Business and Chancery Court is a court of record.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-102(3): 78A-5a-103 The Business and Chancery Court is a trial court with limited and statewide jurisdiction over actions and claims as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-102(4): The Business and Chancery Court is of equal status with the district and juvenile courts of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-102(5): The Business and Chancery Court is established as a forum for the resolution of all matters properly brought before the Business and Chancery Court and consistent with applicable constitutional and statutory requirements of due process.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-102(6): The Business and Chancery Court shall have a seal.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-102(7): The judges and clerks of the Business and Chancery Court have the power to administer oaths and affirmations.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103 Concurrent jurisdiction of the Business and Chancery Court -- Exceptions.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1): The Business and Chancery Court has jurisdiction, concurrent with the district court, over an action:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(a): seeking monetary damages of at least $300,000 or seeking solely equitable relief; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i): with a claim arising from:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(A): a breach of a contract;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(B): a breach of a fiduciary duty;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(C): a dispute over the internal affairs or governance of a business organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(D): the sale, merger, or dissolution of a business organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(E): the sale of substantially all of the assets of a business organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(F): the receivership or liquidation of a business organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(G): a dispute over liability or indemnity between or among owners of the same business organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(H): a dispute over liability or indemnity of an officer or owner of a business organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(I): a tortious or unlawful act committed against a business organization, including an act of unfair competition, tortious interference, or misrepresentation or fraud;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(J): a dispute between a business organization and an insurer regarding a commercial insurance policy;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(K): a contract or transaction governed by Title 70A, Uniform Commercial Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(L): the misappropriation of trade secrets under Title 13, Chapter 24, Uniform Trade Secrets Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(M): the misappropriation of intellectual property;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(N): a noncompete agreement, a nonsolicitation agreement, or a nondisclosure or confidentiality agreement, regardless of whether the agreement is oral or written;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(O): a relationship between a franchisor and a franchisee;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(P): the purchase or sale of a security or an allegation of security fraud;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(Q): a dispute over a blockchain, blockchain technology, or a decentralized autonomous organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(R): a violation of Title 76, Chapter 10, Part 31, Utah Antitrust Act; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(i)(S): a contract with a forum selection clause for a chancery, business, or commercial court of this state or any other state;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(ii): with a malpractice claim concerning services that a professional provided to a business organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(iii): that is a shareholder derivative action; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(1)(b)(iv): seeking a declaratory judgment as described in Title 78B, Chapter 6, Part 4, Declaratory Judgments.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(2): Except as provided in Subsection (3), the Business and Chancery Court may exercise supplemental jurisdiction over any claim in an action that is within the jurisdiction of the Business and Chancery Court under Subsection (1) if the claim arises from the same set of facts or circumstances as the action.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3): The Business and Chancery Court may not exercise supplemental jurisdiction over:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a): any claim arising from:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(i): a consumer contract;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(ii): a personal injury, including a personal injury relating to or arising out of health care rendered or which should have been rendered by the health care provider;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(iii): a violation of Title 13, Chapter 7, Civil Rights;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(iv): Title 20A, Election Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(v): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(vi): Title 78B, Chapter 6, Part 1, Utah Adoption Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(vii): Title 78B, Chapter 6, Part 5, Eminent Domain;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(viii): Title 78B, Chapter 6, Part 8, Forcible Entry and Detainer, unless the claim is brought against a commercial tenant;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(ix): Title 78B, Chapter 7, Protective Orders and Stalking Injunctions;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(x): Title 78B, Chapter 13, Utah Uniform Child Custody Jurisdiction and Enforcement Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(xi): Title 78B, Chapter 14, Utah Uniform Interstate Family Support Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(xii): Title 78B, Chapter 15, Utah Uniform Parentage Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(xiii): Title 78B, Chapter 16, Utah Uniform Child Abduction Prevention Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(xiv): Title 78B, Chapter 20, Uniform Deployed Parents Custody, Parent-time, and Visitation Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(a)(xv): Title 81, Utah Domestic Relations Code; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(b): any action in which a governmental entity is a party; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(3)(c): any criminal matter, unless the criminal matter is an act or omission of contempt that occurs in an action before the Business and Chancery Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(4): Notwithstanding Subsection (3), the Business and Chancery Court may exercise supplemental jurisdiction over a claim that is barred under Subsection (3):
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(4)(a): if the claim is a compulsory counterclaim;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(4)(b): if there would be a material risk of inconsistent outcomes if the claim were tried in a separate action; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(4)(c): solely to resolve a request for a provisional remedy related to the claim before the Business and Chancery Court transfers the claim as described in Subsection (5).
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(5): If an action contains a claim for which the Business and Chancery Court may not exercise supplemental jurisdiction under this section, the Business and Chancery Court shall bifurcate the action and transfer any claim for which the Business and Chancery Court does not have jurisdiction to a court with jurisdiction under Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(6): Before the Business and Chancery Court transfers a claim as described in Subsection (5), the Business and Chancery Court may resolve:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(6)(a): all claims for which the Business and Chancery Court has jurisdiction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-103(6)(b): any request for a provisional remedy related to a claim that is being transferred.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-104 Trier of fact and law -- Demand for jury trial.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-104(1): The Business and Chancery Court is the trier of fact and law in an action before the Business and Chancery Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-104(2): 78A-5a-103 Notwithstanding Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-104(2)(a): a party to the action demands a trial by jury in accordance with the Utah Rules of Business and Chancery Procedure; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-104(2)(b): the Business and Chancery Court finds the party that made the demand has the right to a trial by jury on a claim in the action.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-104(3): Before the Business and Chancery Court transfers an action or a claim under Subsection (2), the Business and Chancery Court may:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-104(3)(a): bifurcate the action and resolve all claims in which the party does not have a right to a trial by jury; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-104(3)(b): administrate and adjudicate the action or claim being transferred prior to a trial by jury, including any pleading, provisional remedy, discovery, or motion.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-105 Venue for the Business and Chancery Court.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-105(1): Title 78B, Chapter 3a, Venue for Civil Actions
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-105(2): Any requirement in the Utah Code to file or bring an action in a specific district or county does not apply to an action brought in the Business and Chancery Court.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-201 Judges of the Business and Chancery Court -- Terms.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-201(1): A judge of the Business and Chancery Court is appointed to initially serve until the first general election held more than three years after the day on which the appointment is effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-201(2): (1) After the initial term described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-201(3): A judge of the Business and Chancery Court whose term expires may serve, upon request of the Judicial Council, until a successor is appointed and qualified.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202 Presiding judge - Associate presiding judge -- Compensation -- Powers -- Duties.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(1)(a): The judges of the Business and Chancery Court shall elect a presiding judge from among the members of the court by majority vote of all judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(1)(b): The presiding judge shall receive $2,000 per annum as additional compensation for the period served as presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(2): The presiding judge has the following authority and responsibilities, consistent with the policies of the Judicial Council:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(2)(a): implementing policies of the Judicial Council; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(2)(b): exercising powers and performing administrative duties as authorized by the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(3)(a): If the Business and Chancery Court has more than two judges, the judges of the Business and Chancery Court may elect an associate presiding judge from among the members of the court by majority vote of all judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(3)(b): The associate presiding judge shall receive $1,000 per annum as additional compensation for the period served as associate presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(4)(a): When the presiding judge is unavailable, the associate presiding judge shall assume the responsibilities of the presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-202(4)(b): The associate presiding judge shall perform other duties assigned by the presiding judge.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203 Administrative system -- Case management -- Clerk of the court -- Employees.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(1)(a): There is established the State Business and Chancery Court Administrative System.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(1)(b): The Judicial Council shall administer the operation of the State Business and Chancery Court Administrative System.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(2): The Business and Chancery Court shall develop a case management system that:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(2)(a): ensures judicial accountability for the just and timely disposition of cases; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(2)(b): provides each judge of the Business and Chancery Court a full judicial workload that accommodates differences in the subject matter or complexity of cases assigned to different judges of the Business and Chancery Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(3): The clerk of the Business and Chancery Court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(3)(a): take charge of and safely keep the court seal;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(3)(b): take charge of and safely keep or dispose of all books, papers, and records filed or deposited with the clerk and all other records required by law or the rules of the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(3)(c): issue all notices, processes, and summonses as authorized by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(3)(d): keep a record of all proceedings, actions, orders, judgments, and decrees of the court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(3)(e): supervise the deputy clerks as required to perform the duties of the clerk's office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(3)(f): perform other duties as required by the presiding judge, the business and chancery court administrator, applicable law, and the rules of the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-203(4): All employees, except judges of the Business and Chancery Court, are selected, promoted, and discharged through the state courts personnel system for the Business and Chancery Court under the direction and rules of the Judicial Council.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-204 Location of the Business and Chancery Court -- Court facilities -- Costs.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-204(1): The Business and Chancery Court may perform any of the Business and Chancery Court's functions in any location within the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-204(2): The Judicial Council shall provide, from appropriations made by the Legislature, court space suitable for the conduct of court business for the Business and Chancery Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-204(3): The Judicial Council may, in order to carry out the Judicial Council's obligation to provide facilities for the Business and Chancery Court, lease space to be used by the Business and Chancery Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-204(4): A lease or reimbursement for the Business and Chancery Court must comply with the standards of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management that are applicable to state agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-204(5): The cost of salaries, travel, and training required for the discharge of the duties of judges, secretaries of judges or court executives, court executives, and court reporters for the Business and Chancery Court are paid from appropriations made by the Legislature.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-205 Court sessions.
------------------------------------------------
The Business and Chancery Court shall hold court at least once in each quarter of the year.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-301 Publication of decisions and orders.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
The Business and Chancery Court shall:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-301(1): publish all final decisions and orders issued by the Business and Chancery Court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-301(2): make all final decisions and orders public on the Utah Courts' website.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-5a-302 Tentative ruling before oral argument.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
The Business and Chancery Court shall provide the parties with a proposed ruling on each motion within 48 hours before the day on which oral argument is held on the motion.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Chapter 6 - Juvenile Court
************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as "Juvenile Court."

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-101.5 Definitions.
----------------------------------------------
The terms defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102 Establishment of juvenile court -- Organization and status of court -- Purpose.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(1): There is established a juvenile court for the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(2): 80-2a-202; Part 4a, Adult Criminal Proceedings; Title 80, Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings; Title 80, Chapter 4, Termination and Restoration of Parental Rights; Title 80, Chapter 6, Juvenile Justice; Title 77, Utah Code of Criminal Procedure
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(2)(a): The juvenile court is a court of record.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(2)(b): The juvenile court shall have a seal.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(2)(c): The juvenile court's judges, clerks, and referees have the power to administer oaths and affirmations.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(2)(d): 80-2a-202; Part 4a, Adult Criminal Proceedings; Title 80, Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings; Title 80, Chapter 4, Termination and Restoration of Parental Rights; Title 80, Chapter 6, Juvenile Justice; Title 77, Utah Code of Criminal Procedure The juvenile court has the authority to issue search warrants, subpoenas, or investigative subpoenas under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(3): The juvenile court is of equal status with the district courts of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(4): The juvenile court is established as a forum for the resolution of all matters properly brought before the juvenile court, consistent with applicable constitutional and statutory requirements of due process.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(5): The purpose of the court under this chapter is to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(5)(a): promote public safety and individual accountability by the imposition of appropriate sanctions on persons who have committed acts in violation of law;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(5)(b): order appropriate measures to promote guidance and control, preferably in the minor's own home, as an aid in the prevention of future unlawful conduct and the development of responsible citizenship;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(5)(c): where appropriate, order rehabilitation, reeducation, and treatment for persons who have committed acts bringing them within the court's jurisdiction;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(5)(d): adjudicate matters that relate to minors who are beyond parental or adult control and to establish appropriate authority over these minors by means of placement and control orders;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(5)(e): adjudicate matters that relate to abused, neglected, and dependent children and to provide care and protection for minors by placement, protection, and custody orders;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(5)(f): remove a minor from parental custody only where the minor's safety or welfare, or the public safety, may not otherwise be adequately safeguarded; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-102(5)(g): consistent with the ends of justice, act in the best interests of the minor in all cases and preserve and strengthen family ties.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-201 Judges of juvenile court -- Appointments -- Terms.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-201(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-201(1)(a): A judge of the juvenile court shall be appointed initially to serve until the first general election held more than three years after the day on which the appointment is effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-201(1)(b): (1)(a) After the initial term described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-201(2): A juvenile court judge whose term expires may serve, upon request of the Judicial Council, until a successor is appointed and qualified.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-202 Sessions of juvenile court.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-202(1): In each county, regular juvenile court sessions shall be held at a place designated by the judge or judges of the juvenile court district, with the approval of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-202(2): Juvenile court sessions shall be held in each county when the presiding judge of the juvenile court directs, except that a judge of the district may hold court in any county within the district at any time if required by the urgency of the case.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203 Board of Juvenile Court Judges -- Composition -- Purpose -- Presiding judge -- Associate presiding judge.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1): 78A-6-102(5); Title 80, Utah Juvenile Code
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(a): The Judicial Council shall, by rule, establish a Board of Juvenile Court Judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(b): The board shall establish general policies for the operation of the juvenile courts and uniform rules and forms governing practice, consistent with the provisions of this chapter, the rules of the Judicial Council, and the rules of the Supreme Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(c): 78A-6-102(5)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(c)(i): 78A-6-102(5) The board may receive and expend any funds that may become available from the federal government or private sources to carry out any of the purposes described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(c)(ii): The board may meet any federal requirements that are conditions precedent to receiving the funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(c)(iii): The board may cooperate with the federal government in a program for training personnel employed, or preparing for employment, by the juvenile court and may receive and expend funds from federal or state sources or from private donations for these purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(c)(iv): Funds donated or paid to the juvenile court by private sources for the purpose of compensatory service programs are nonlapsing.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(c)(v): The board may:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(c)(v)(A): contract with public or nonprofit institutions of higher learning for the training of personnel;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(c)(v)(B): conduct short-term training courses of the board's own and hire experts on a temporary basis for this purpose; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(c)(v)(C): cooperate with the Division of Child and Family Services and other state departments or agencies in personnel training programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(d): Title 80, Utah Juvenile Code The board may contract, on behalf of the juvenile court, with the United States Forest Service or other agencies or departments of the federal government or with agencies or departments of other states for the care and placement of minors adjudicated under
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(1)(e): The powers to contract and expend funds are subject to budgetary control and procedures as provided by law.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(2): Under the direction of the presiding officer of the council, the chair shall supervise the juvenile courts to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(2)(a): ensure uniform adherence to law and to the rules and forms adopted by the Supreme Court and Judicial Council; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(2)(b): promote the proper and efficient functioning of the juvenile courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(3)(a): In judicial districts having more than one juvenile court judge, the juvenile court judges shall elect one judge of the district to the office of presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(3)(b): The presiding judge shall receive $2,000 per annum as additional compensation for the period served as presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(4)(a): In judicial districts having more than two juvenile court judges, the juvenile court judges may elect one judge of the district to the office of associate presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(4)(b): The associate presiding judge shall receive $1,000 per annum as additional compensation for the period served as associate presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(5): The presiding juvenile court judge, in accordance with the policies of the Judicial Council, shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(5)(a): implement policies of the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(5)(b): exercise powers and perform administrative duties as authorized by the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(5)(c): manage the judicial business of the district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(5)(d): call and preside over meetings of juvenile court judges of the district.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(6)(a): When the presiding judge is unavailable, the associate presiding judge shall assume the responsibilities of the presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-203(6)(b): The associate presiding judge shall perform other duties assigned by the presiding judge.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-204 Administrator of juvenile court -- Appointment -- Qualifications -- Powers and duties.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-204(1): With the approval of the board, the state court administrator shall appoint a chief administrative officer of the juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-204(2): The chief administrative officer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-204(2)(a): be selected on the basis of professional ability and experience in the field of public administration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-204(2)(b): possess an understanding of court procedures and the nature and significance of probation services and other court services.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-211 Courtrooms -- Physical facilities.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-211(1): Suitable courtrooms and office space in each county shall be provided or made available to the juvenile court by the county for the hearing of cases, except in counties where the state has provided courtrooms and offices as needed.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-211(2): Equipment and supplies for the use of the judges, officers, and employees of the juvenile court and the cost of maintaining the juvenile courts shall be paid from the General Fund or other funds for those purposes.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-212 Information supplied to the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-212(1): A juvenile probation officer shall render full and complete cooperation to the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services in supplying the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services with all pertinent information relating to a juvenile offender committed to the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-212(2): Information under Subsection (1) includes prior criminal history, social history, psychological evaluations, and identifying information specified by the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-350 Venue -- Dismissal without adjudication on merits.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-350(1): 80-6-1001.2 Notwithstanding Title 78B, Chapter 3a, Venue for Civil Actions, a proceeding for a minor's case in the juvenile court shall be commenced in the court of the district in which:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-350(1)(a): 80-6-1001.2 except as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-350(1)(a)(i): the minor is living or found; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-350(1)(a)(ii): the alleged offense occurred; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-350(1)(b): for any other proceeding, the minor is living or found.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-350(2): If a party seeks to transfer a case to another district after a petition has been filed in the juvenile court, the juvenile court may transfer the case in accordance with the Utah Rules of Juvenile Procedure.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-350(3): The dismissal of a petition in one district where the dismissal is without prejudice and where there has been no adjudication upon the merits may not preclude refiling within the same district or another district where there is venue for the case.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351 Summons -- Service and process -- Issuance and contents -- Notice to absent parent or guardian -- Emergency medical or surgical treatment -- Compulsory process for attendance of witnesses when authorized.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(1)(a): After a petition is filed in the juvenile court, the juvenile court shall promptly issue a summons, unless the juvenile court directs that a further investigation is needed.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(1)(b): A summons is not required for a person who:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(1)(b)(i): appears voluntarily; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(1)(b)(ii): files a written waiver of service with the clerk of the court at or before the hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(2): (1)(a) A summons under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(2)(a): the name of the court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(2)(b): the title of the proceedings; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(2)(c): except for a published summons, a brief statement of the substance of the allegations in the petition.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(3): A published summons shall state:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(3)(a): that a proceeding concerning the minor is pending in the court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(3)(b): an adjudication will be made.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(4): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(4)(a): (1)(a) A summons under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(4)(a)(ii)(A): appear personally; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(4)(a)(ii)(B): bring the minor before the court at a time and place stated.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(4)(b): If the minor is a child and a person summoned is not the parent or guardian of the minor, the juvenile court shall issue the summons to the minor's parent or guardian, as the case may be, notifying the parent or guardian of the pendency of the case and of the time and place set for the hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(5): A summons may be issued requiring the appearance of any other person whose presence the juvenile court finds necessary.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-351(6): 80-6-201; 80-2a-202; 80-6-202 If it appears to the juvenile court that the welfare of the minor or of the public requires that the minor be taken into temporary custody under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352 Appearances -- Parents, guardian, or custodian to appear with minor or child -- Failure to appear -- Warrant of arrest, when authorized -- Parent's, guardian's, or custodian's employer to grant time off -- Appointment of guardian ad litem.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(1): If a person is required to appear in a proceeding in the juvenile court and the person fails, without reasonable cause, to appear before the juvenile court, the juvenile court may issue a bench warrant to produce the person in court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(2): If a child is required to appear in juvenile court, the child's parent, guardian, or custodian shall appear with the child in the juvenile court, unless the child's parent, guardian, or custodian is excused by the juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(3)(a): A child's parent, guardian, or custodian may request permission from the parent's, guardian's, or custodian's employer to leave the workplace for the purpose of attending court if the parent, guardian, or custodian is notified by the juvenile court that the child is required to appear before the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(3)(b): An employer must grant the parent, guardian, or custodian permission to leave the workplace with or without pay if the parent, guardian, or custodian requests permission at least seven days in advance or within 24 hours of the parent, guardian, or custodian receiving notice of the hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(4): 80-6-203; (4)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(4)(a): 80-6-203 If a parent, guardian, custodian or other person to whom a child is released, signed a written promise to appear and bring the child to juvenile court under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(4)(b): (4)(a) A willful failure to perform the promise described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(5)(a): A juvenile court shall make every effort to ensure the presence of the parent, guardian, or custodian of a child at all hearings through the use of a warrant of arrest, if necessary, or by other means.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(5)(b): A juvenile court may appoint a guardian ad litem whenever necessary for the welfare of a child, regardless of whether the child's parent or guardian is present at the juvenile court proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(6): A juvenile court may issue a warrant for a child's parent, guardian, or custodian if:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(6)(a): a summons is issued but cannot be served;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(6)(b): it appears to the juvenile court that the person to be served will not obey the summons; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-352(6)(c): serving the summons will be ineffectual.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353 Contempt -- Penalty -- Enforcement of fine, fee, or restitution.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(1): An individual who willfully violates or refuses to obey any order of the juvenile court may be proceeded against for contempt of court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(2): If a juvenile court finds an individual who is 18 years old or older in contempt of court, the juvenile court may impose sanctions on the individual in accordance with Title 78B, Chapter 6, Part 3, Contempt.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(3): 80-6-702; 80-6-704; 80-6-709 Except as otherwise provided in Subsection (4), if a juvenile court finds a child in contempt of court, the juvenile court may:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(3)(a): 80-6-702 place the child on probation in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(3)(b): 80-6-704 order the child to detention, or an alternative to detention, in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(3)(c): 80-6-709 require the child to pay a fine or fee in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(4)(a): The juvenile court may only order a child to secure detention under Subsection (3)(b) for no longer than 72 hours, excluding weekends and legal holidays.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(4)(b): The juvenile court may not suspend all or part of an order to secure detention upon compliance with conditions imposed by the juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(4)(c): The juvenile court may not enforce a disposition under Subsection (3)(c) through an order for detention, a community-based program, or secure care.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(5): On the sole basis of a child's absence from placement, a juvenile court may not hold a child in contempt under this section if the child:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(5)(a): is in the legal custody of the Division of Child and Family Services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-353(5)(b): is missing, has been abducted, or has run away.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-354 Hearings -- Minors cases heard separately from adult cases -- Minor or parents or custodian heard separately -- Continuance of hearing.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-354(1): A hearing for a minor's case shall be held before the juvenile court without a jury and may be conducted in an informal manner.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-354(2): Title 80, Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings; Chapter 4, Termination and Restoration of Parental Rights; Chapter 6, Juvenile Justice
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-354(2)(a): Title 80, Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings; Chapter 4, Termination and Restoration of Parental Rights; Chapter 6, Juvenile Justice A minor's case under
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-354(2)(b): The minor or the minor's parent or guardian may be heard separately when considered necessary by the juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-354(2)(c): A hearing may be continued to a date specified by court order.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-355 Exchange of information with agency or institution having legal custody.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-355(1): If legal custody of a minor is vested in an institution or agency, the juvenile court shall transmit, with the court order, copies of the social study, any clinical reports, and other information pertinent to the care and treatment of the minor to the institution or agency with legal custody of the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-355(2): The institution or agency shall give the juvenile court any information concerning the minor that the juvenile court may at any time require.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356 Child support obligation when custody of a child is vested in an individual or institution.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(1)(a): "Office" means the Office of Recovery Services.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(1)(b): "State custody" means that a child is in the custody of a state department, division, or agency, including secure care.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(2): Under this section, a juvenile court may not issue a child support order against an individual unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(2)(a): the individual is served with notice that specifies the date and time of a hearing to determine the financial support of a specified child;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(2)(b): the individual makes a voluntary appearance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(2)(c): the individual submits a waiver of service.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(3): Except as provided in Subsection (11), when a juvenile court places a child in state custody or if the guardianship of the child has been granted to another party and an agreement for a guardianship subsidy has been signed by the guardian, the juvenile court:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(3)(a): shall order the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual to pay child support for each month the child is in state custody or cared for under a grant of guardianship;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(3)(b): shall inform the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual, verbally and in writing, of the requirement to pay child support in accordance with Title 81, Chapter 6, Child Support; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(3)(c): may refer the establishment of a child support order to the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(4): When a juvenile court chooses to refer a case to the office to determine support obligation amounts in accordance with Title 81, Chapter 6, Child Support, the juvenile court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(4)(a): make the referral within three working days after the day on which the juvenile court holds the hearing described in Subsection (2)(a); and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(4)(b): inform the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual of:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(4)(b)(i): the requirement to contact the office within 30 days after the day on which the juvenile court holds the hearing described in Subsection (2)(a); and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(4)(b)(ii): the penalty described in Subsection (6) for failure to contact the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(5): Liability for child support ordered under Subsection (3) shall accrue:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(5)(a): except as provided in Subsection (5)(b), beginning on day 61 after the day on which the juvenile court holds the hearing described in Subsection (2)(a) if there is no existing child support order for the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(5)(b): beginning on the day the child is removed from the child's home, including time spent in detention or sheltered care, if the child is removed after having been returned to the child's home from state custody.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(6)(a): If the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual contacts the office within 30 days after the day on which the court holds the hearing described in Subsection (2)(a), the child support order may not include a judgment for past due support for more than two months.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(6)(b): Notwithstanding Subsections (5) and (6)(a), the juvenile court may order the liability of support to begin to accrue from the date of the proceeding referenced in Subsection (3) if:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(6)(b)(i): the court informs the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual, as described in Subsection (4)(b), and the parent, guardian, or other obligated individual fails to contact the office within 30 days after the day on which the court holds the hearing described in Subsection (2)(a); and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(6)(b)(ii): the office took reasonable steps under the circumstances to contact the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual within 30 days after the last day on which the parent, guardian, or other obligated individual was required to contact the office to facilitate the establishment of a child support order.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(6)(c): For purposes of Subsection (6)(b)(ii), the office is presumed to have taken reasonable steps if the office:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(6)(c)(i): has a signed, returned receipt for a certified letter mailed to the address of the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual regarding the requirement that a child support order be established; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(6)(c)(ii): has had a documented conversation, whether by telephone or in person, with the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual regarding the requirement that a child support order be established.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(7): 26B-9-219 In collecting arrears, the office shall comply with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(8)(a): Unless a court orders otherwise, the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual shall pay the child support to the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(8)(b): The clerk of the juvenile court, the office, or the department and the department's divisions shall have authority to receive periodic payments for the care and maintenance of the child, such as social security payments or railroad retirement payments made in the name of or for the benefit of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(9): 26B-9-111 An existing child support order payable to a parent or other individual shall be assigned to the department as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(10): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(10)(a): Subsections (4) through (9) do not apply if legal custody of a child is vested by the juvenile court in an individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(10)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(10)(b)(i): If legal custody of a child is vested by the juvenile court in an individual, the court may order the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual to pay child support to the individual in whom custody is vested.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(10)(b)(ii): In the same proceeding, the juvenile court shall inform the child's parent, guardian, or other obligated individual, verbally and in writing, of the requirement to pay child support in accordance with Title 81, Chapter 6, Child Support.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(11): The juvenile court may not order an individual to pay child support for a child in state custody if:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(11)(a): the individual's only form of income is a government-issued disability benefit;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(11)(b): the benefit described in Subsection (11)(a) is issued because of the individual's disability, and not the child's disability; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(11)(c): the individual provides the juvenile court and the office evidence that the individual meets the requirements of Subsections (11)(a) and (b).
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(12): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(12)(a): The child's parent or another obligated individual is not responsible for child support for the period of time that the child is removed from the child's home by the Division of Child and Family Services if:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(12)(a)(i): the juvenile court finds that there were insufficient grounds for the removal of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(12)(a)(ii): the child is returned to the home of the child's parent or guardian based on the finding described in Subsection (12)(a)(i).
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(12)(b): If the juvenile court finds insufficient grounds for the removal of the child under Subsection (12)(a), but that the child is to remain in state custody, the juvenile court shall order that the child's parent or another obligated individual is responsible for child support beginning on the day on which it became improper to return the child to the home of the child's parent or guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(13): After the juvenile court or the office establishes an individual's child support obligation ordered under Subsection (3), the office shall waive the obligation without further order of the juvenile court if:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(13)(a): the individual's child support obligation is established in accordance with a low income table described in Title 81, Chapter 6, Part 3, Child Support Tables; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(13)(b): the individual's only source of income is a means-tested, income replacement payment of aid, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(13)(b)(i): cash assistance provided under Title 35A, Chapter 3, Part 3, Family Employment Program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-356(13)(b)(ii): cash benefits received under General Assistance, social security income, or social security disability income.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-450 Criminal information for an adult in juvenile court.

A county attorney or district attorney may file a criminal information in the juvenile court charging an adult for:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-6-450(1): 32B-4-403 unlawful sale or furnishing of an alcoholic product to minors in violation of Section

Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Chapter 7 - Justice Court
***********************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.1 Definitions for chapter.
----------------------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.1(1): 53G-8-211 "Adult high school student" means an individual who:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.1(1)(a): is 18 years old and enrolled in high school at the time of the offense;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.1(1)(b): is under 21 years old at the time of all court proceedings; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.1(1)(c): 53G-8-211 committed the offense on school property where the individual is enrolled:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.1(1)(c)(i): when school was in session; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.1(1)(c)(ii): 53G-8-211 during a school-sponsored activity, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.1(2): "Body of water" includes any stream, river, lake, or reservoir, whether natural or man-made.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.1(3): 77-36-1 "Domestic violence offense" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.1(4): "Minor" means an individual who is 16 or 17 years old.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5 Creation of justice court -- Not of record -- Independent branch of local government -- Classes of justice courts.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(1)(a): Under Article VIII, Section 1, Utah Constitution, there is created a court not of record known as the justice court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(1)(b): The judges of this court are justice court judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(2): 78A-1-101 A justice court is:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(2)(a): 78A-1-101 a court of this state in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(2)(b): a part of the state judiciary even though the justice court is funded and staffed by a municipality or county; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(2)(c): independent from the other branches of government for a municipality or county.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(3): A justice court may not be treated as part of the executive or legislative branches or offices of a municipality or county.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(4): A municipality or county may only operate a justice court as authorized by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(5): Justice courts shall be divided into the following classes:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(5)(a): Class I: 501 or more case filings per month;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(5)(b): Class II: 201-500 case filings per month;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(5)(c): Class III: 61-200 case filings per month; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-101.5(5)(d): Class IV: 60 or fewer case filings per month.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102 Establishment of justice courts.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(1): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(1)(a): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act As used in this section, to "create a justice court" means to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(1)(a)(i): establish a justice court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(1)(a)(ii): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act establish a justice court under
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(1)(b): For the purposes of this section, if more than one municipality or county is collectively proposing to create a justice court, the class of the justice court shall be determined by the total citations or cases filed within the territorial jurisdiction of the proposed justice court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(2): 78A-7-103 A municipality or county of the first or second class may create a justice court by filing a written declaration with the Judicial Council on or before July 1 at least two years before the effective date of the election.  Upon demonstration of compliance with operating standards as established by statute and the Judicial Council, the Judicial Council shall certify the creation of the justice court under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(3): 78A-7-103
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(3)(a): A municipality or county of the third, fourth, or fifth class may create a justice court by demonstrating the need for the justice court and filing a written declaration with the Judicial Council on or before July 1 at least one year before the effective date of the election.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(3)(b): A municipality or county creating a justice court shall demonstrate to the Judicial Council that a justice court is needed.  In evaluating the need for a justice court, the Judicial Council shall consider factors of population, case filings, public convenience, availability of law enforcement agencies and court support services, proximity to other courts, and any special circumstances.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(3)(c): 78A-7-103 The Judicial Council shall certify the creation of the justice court under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(3)(c)(i): a need exists;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(3)(c)(ii): the municipality or county has filed a timely application; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(3)(c)(iii): the proposed justice court will be in compliance with all of the operating standards established by statute and the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act; (4); 78A-7-123; Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act; (4)(e); (4)(e)(iii); 78A-7-123
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(a): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act A municipality that has a justice court may expand the territorial jurisdiction of the justice court by entering into an agreement under
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(b): (4) A justice court enlarged under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(c): 78A-7-123 A municipality or county seeking to expand the territorial jurisdiction of a justice court shall notify the Judicial Council:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(c)(i): 78A-7-123 no later than the notice period required in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(c)(ii): no later than 180 days before the expanded court seeks to begin operation when the expanded justice court is a result of other circumstances.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(d): The Judicial Council shall certify the expansion of a justice court if it determines that the expanded justice court is in compliance with the operating standards established by statute and the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(e): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act; (4)(e); (4)(e)(iii); 78A-7-123
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(e)(i): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act; (4)(e); (4)(e)(iii) A municipality or county that has a justice court at the time of executing an interlocal agreement, under
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(e)(ii): The municipality or county shall notify the Judicial Council at least 90 days before resuming operations. The municipality or county shall demonstrate that the municipality's or county's justice court will be in compliance with the operating standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(e)(iii): 78A-7-123 If the Judicial Council determines that a justice court will not be in compliance with the operating standards, the Judicial Council shall direct the expanded justice court to continue operation until the Judicial Council is satisfied the municipality's or county's  justice court will meet the operating standards or until the municipality or county dissolves the municipality's or county's justice court in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(4)(e)(iv): If the interlocal agreement includes a municipality or county that did not have a justice court at the time the interlocal agreement was executed, the municipality or county shall notify the Judicial Council at least 180 days before termination of the interlocal agreement. In the notification, the municipality or county shall set forth its intentions in regard to adjudicating offenses committed within the municipality's or county's territorial boundaries. The Judicial Council may require the expanded justice court to continue operation until the Judicial Council is satisfied that the municipality's or county's caseload will be adequately subsumed by another justice court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(5): Upon request from a municipality or county seeking to create a justice court, the Judicial Council may shorten the time required between the municipality's or county's written declaration or election to create a justice court and the effective date of the election.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-102(6): The Judicial Council may by rule provide resources and procedures adequate for the timely disposition of all matters brought before the courts.  The Administrative Office of the Courts and local governments shall cooperate in allocating resources to operate the courts in the most efficient and effective manner based on the allocation of responsibility between courts of record and not of record.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103 Minimum standards of justice courts -- Authority of Judicial Council over justice courts.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Judicial Council shall ensure that:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(1): Title 78B, Chapter 22, Indigent Defense Act procedures include requirements that every municipality or county that establishes or maintains a justice court provide for the following minimum operating standards:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(1)(a): a system to ensure the justice court records all proceedings with a digital audio recording device and maintains the audio recordings for a minimum of one year;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(1)(b): sufficient prosecutors to perform the prosecutorial duties before the justice court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(1)(c): Title 78B, Chapter 22, Indigent Defense Act adequate funding to provide indigent defense services for indigent individuals under
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(1)(d): sufficient local peace officers to provide security for the justice court and to attend to the justice court when required;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(1)(e): sufficient clerical personnel to serve the needs of the justice court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(1)(f): sufficient funds to cover the cost of travel and training expenses of clerical personnel and judges at training sessions mandated by the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(1)(g): adequate courtroom and auxiliary space for the justice court, which need not be specifically constructed for or allocated solely for the justice court when existing facilities adequately serve the purposes of the justice court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(1)(h): for each judge of its justice court, a current copy of the Utah Code, the Utah Court Rules Annotated, the justice court manual published by the state court administrator, the county, city, or town ordinances as appropriate, and other legal reference materials as determined to be necessary by the judge; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(2): the Judicial Council's rules and procedures shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(2)(a): presume that existing justice courts will be recertified at the end of each four-year term if the court continues to meet the minimum requirements for the establishment of a new justice court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(2)(b): authorize the Judicial Council, upon request of a municipality or county or upon its own review, when a justice court does not meet the minimum requirements, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(2)(b)(i): decline recertification of a justice court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(2)(b)(ii): revoke the certification of a justice court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(2)(b)(iii): extend the time for a justice court to comply with the minimum requirements; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-103(2)(b)(iv): suspend rules of the Judicial Council governing justice courts, if the council believes suspending those rules is the appropriate administrative remedy for the justice courts of this state.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106 Original jurisdiction of a justice court -- Territorial jurisdiction -- Transfer of a domestic violence case.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(1): A justice court has original jurisdiction over class B and C misdemeanors, violations of ordinances, and infractions committed within the justice court's territorial jurisdiction by an individual who is 18 years old or older.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2): A justice court has original jurisdiction over the following offenses committed within the justice court's territorial jurisdiction by a minor or an adult high school student:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(a): class C misdemeanor and infraction violations described in Title 53, Chapter 3, Part 2, Driver Licensing Act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(b): class B and C misdemeanor and infraction violations described in:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(b)(i): Title 23A, Wildlife Resources Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(b)(ii): Title 41, Chapter 1a, Motor Vehicle Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(b)(iii): Title 41, Chapter 6a, Traffic Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(b)(iv): Title 41, Chapter 12a, Financial Responsibility of Motor Vehicle Owners and Operators Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(b)(v): Title 41, Chapter 22, Off-highway Vehicles;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(b)(vi): Title 73, Chapter 18, State Boating Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(b)(vii): Title 73, Chapter 18a, Boating - Litter and Pollution Control;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(b)(viii): Title 73, Chapter 18b, Water Safety; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(2)(b)(ix): Title 73, Chapter 18c, Financial Responsibility of Motorboat Owners and Operators Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(3): 78A-5-102(8); 78A-5-102.5; 78A-6-103.5; 73-18-12 Notwithstanding Subsection (1) or (2), a justice court does not have original jurisdiction over:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(3)(a): 78A-5-102(8); 78A-5-102.5; 78A-6-103.5 an offense described in Subsection (1) or (2) if:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(3)(a)(i): 78A-5-102(8); 78A-5-102.5 the district court has exclusive jurisdiction over the offense in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(3)(a)(ii): 78A-6-103.5 the juvenile court has exclusive jurisdiction over the offense in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(3)(b): 73-18-12 the following offenses committed within the justice court's territorial jurisdiction by a minor or an adult high school student:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(3)(b)(i): class B and C misdemeanor violations described in Title 41, Chapter 6a, Part 5, Driving Under the Influence and Reckless Driving; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(3)(b)(ii): 73-18-12 a class B misdemeanor violation described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(4): A justice court has jurisdiction over:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(4)(a): a small claims case under Chapter 8, Small Claims Courts, if a defendant resides in or the debt arose within the territorial jurisdiction of the justice court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(4)(b): a petition for expungement as described in Title 77, Chapter 40a, Expungement of Criminal Records.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5): An offense is committed within the territorial jurisdiction of a justice court if:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(a): conduct constituting an element of the offense or a result constituting an element of the offense occurs within the court's jurisdiction, regardless of whether the conduct or result is itself unlawful;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(b): either an individual  committing an offense or a victim of an offense is located within the court's jurisdiction at the time the offense is committed;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(c): either a cause of injury occurs within the court's jurisdiction or the injury occurs within the court's jurisdiction;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(d): an individual commits any act constituting an element of an inchoate offense within the court's jurisdiction, including an agreement in a conspiracy;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(e): an individual solicits, aids, or abets, or attempts to solicit, aid, or abet another individual in the planning or commission of an offense within the court's jurisdiction;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(f): the investigation of the offense does not readily indicate in which court's jurisdiction the offense occurred, and:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(f)(i): the offense is committed upon or in any railroad car, vehicle, watercraft, or aircraft passing within the court's jurisdiction;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(f)(ii): the offense is committed on or in any body of water bordering on or within this state if the territorial limits of the justice court are adjacent to the body of water;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(f)(iii): an individual who commits theft exercises control over the affected property within the court's jurisdiction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(f)(iv): the offense is committed on or near the boundary of the court's jurisdiction;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(g): the offense consists of an unlawful communication that was initiated or received within the court's jurisdiction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(5)(h): jurisdiction is otherwise specifically provided by law.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(6): If a defendant in a criminal case before a justice court is a minor, the justice court may transfer the case to the juvenile court for further proceedings if the justice court determines and the juvenile court concurs that the best interests of the defendant would be served by the continuing jurisdiction of the juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(7): (7)(b); (7)(c)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(7)(a): If a justice court has jurisdiction over a criminal action involving a domestic violence offense and the criminal action is set for trial, the prosecuting attorney or the defendant may file a notice of transfer in the justice court to transfer the criminal action from the justice court to the district court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(7)(b): If a prosecuting attorney files a notice of transfer, the prosecuting attorney shall certify in the notice of transfer that the prosecuting attorney, or a representative from the prosecuting attorney's office, has consulted with, or notified, all of the alleged victims about transferring the criminal action to the district court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(7)(c): (7)(b); (7)(c) The justice court shall transfer a criminal action to the district court if the justice court receives a notice of transfer from:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(7)(c)(i): the defendant as described in Subsection (7)(b); or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-106(7)(c)(ii): (7)(b); (7)(c) the prosecuting attorney as described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-118(9)(a): the decision results in immediate dismissal of the case; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-118(9)(b): the hearing de novo was on a pretrial order and the parties and the district court agree to have the district court retain jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-118(10): The district court shall retain jurisdiction over the case on trial de novo.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-118(11): The decision of the district court is final and may not be appealed unless the district court rules on the constitutionality of a statute or ordinance.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-122(4)(b): 78A-2-602; 78A-7-301 80% shall be remitted to the state treasurer to be distributed as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-122(4)(b)(i): 62.5% to the treasurer of the county in which the justice court which remitted the amount is located;
