Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123 Dissolution of justice courts.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(1)(a): The county or municipality shall obtain legislative approval to dissolve a justice court if the caseload from that court would fall to the district court upon dissolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(1)(b): To obtain approval of the Legislature, the governing authority of the municipality or county shall petition the Legislature to adopt a joint resolution to approve the dissolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(1)(c): The municipality or county shall provide notice to the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(1)(d): Notice of intent to dissolve a Class I or Class II justice court to the Judicial Council shall be given not later than July 1 two years prior to the general session in which the county or municipality intends to seek legislative approval.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(1)(e): Notice of intent to dissolve a Class III or Class IV justice court to the Judicial Council shall be given not later than July 1 immediately prior to the general session in which the county or municipality intends to seek legislative approval.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(2)(a): A county or municipality shall give notice of intent to dissolve a justice court to the Judicial Council if the caseload of that court would fall to the county justice court.  A municipality shall also give notice to the county of its intent to dissolve a justice court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(2)(b): Notice of intent to dissolve a Class I or Class II court shall be given by July 1 at least two years prior to the effective date of the dissolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(2)(c): Notice of intent to dissolve a Class III or Class IV court shall be given by July 1 at least one year prior to the effective date of the dissolution.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-123(3): Upon request from a municipality or county seeking to dissolve a justice court, the Judicial Council may shorten the time required between the city's or county's notice of intent to dissolve a justice court and the effective date of the dissolution.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201 Justice court judge eligibility -- Mandatory retirement.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(1): A justice court judge shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(1)(a): a citizen of the United States;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(1)(b): 25 years old or older;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(1)(c): a resident of Utah for at least three years immediately preceding the judge's appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(1)(d): upon appointment or within a reasonable time after appointment, a resident of the county, an adjacent county, or the judicial district in which the justice court is located; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(1)(e): a qualified voter of the county in which the judge resides.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(2)(a): On and after May 3, 2023, a justice court judge shall have a degree from a law school that makes one eligible to apply for admission to a bar in any state.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(2)(b): (2)(a) A justice court judge holding office on May 3, 2023, who does not meet the qualification described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(3): (2) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(4): A justice court judge shall be a person who has demonstrated maturity of judgment, integrity, and the ability to understand and apply appropriate law with impartiality.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(5): A justice court judge shall retire upon attaining the age of 75 years.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(6): (2)(a); (2)(a) If there are not at least two applicants for a justice court judge position who meet the requirement of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(6)(a): re-advertise the position; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-201(6)(b): (2)(a) accept applications from individuals who do not meet the requirement of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202 Justice court judges to be appointed -- Procedure.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1): 10-3b-103 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(a): 10-3b-103 "Local government executive" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(a)(i): for a county:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(a)(i)(A): the chair of the county commission in a county operating under the county commission or expanded county commission form of county government;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(a)(i)(B): the county executive in a county operating under the county executive-council form of county government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(a)(i)(C): the county manager in a county operating under the council-manager form of county government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(a)(ii): 10-3b-103 for a city or town:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(a)(ii)(A): the mayor of the city or town; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(a)(ii)(B): 10-3b-103 the city manager, in the council-manager form of government described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(b): "Local legislative body" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(b)(i): for a county, the county commission or county council; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(1)(b)(ii): for a city or town, the council of the city or town.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(a): There is created in each county a county justice court nominating commission to review applicants and make recommendations to the appointing authority for a justice court position.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(b): The commission shall be convened when a new justice court judge position is created or when a vacancy in an existing court occurs for a justice court located within the county.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(c): Membership of the justice court nominating commission shall be as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(c)(i): one member appointed by:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(c)(i)(A): the county commission if the county has a county commission form of government; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(c)(i)(B): the county executive if the county has an executive-council form of government;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(c)(ii): one member appointed by the municipalities in the counties as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(c)(ii)(A): if the county has only one municipality, appointment shall be made by the governing authority of that municipality; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(c)(ii)(B): if the county has more than one municipality, appointment shall be made by a municipal selection committee composed of the mayors of each municipality in the county;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(c)(iii): one member appointed by the county bar association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(c)(iv): two members appointed by the governing authority of the jurisdiction where the judicial office is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(d)(i): If there is no county bar association, the member in Subsection (2)(c)(iii) shall be appointed by the regional bar association.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(d)(ii): If no regional bar association exists, the state bar association shall make the appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(e): Members appointed under Subsections (2)(c)(i) and (ii) may not be the appointing authority or an elected official of a county or municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(f): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(f)(i): Except as provided in Subsection (2)(f)(ii), the nominating commission shall submit at least three names to the appointing authority of the jurisdiction expected to be served by the judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(f)(ii): If there are fewer than three applicants for a justice court vacancy, the nominating commission shall submit all qualified applicants to the appointing authority of the jurisdiction expected to be served by the judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(f)(iii): The local government executive shall appoint a judge from the list submitted and the appointment ratified by the local legislative body.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(g): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(g)(i): The state court administrator shall provide staff to the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(2)(g)(ii): The Judicial Council shall establish rules and procedures for the conduct of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(3): 63G-30-102
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(3)(a): 63G-30-102 A judicial vacancy for a justice court shall be announced:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(3)(a)(i): as an employment opportunity on the Utah Courts' website;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(3)(a)(ii): in an email to the members of the Utah State Bar; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(3)(a)(iii): 63G-30-102 for the justice court's jurisdiction, as a class A notice under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(3)(b): A judicial vacancy for a justice court may also be advertised through other appropriate means.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(4): Selection of candidates shall be based on compliance with the requirements for office and competence to serve as a judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(5)(a): Once selected, every prospective justice court judge shall attend an orientation seminar conducted under the direction of the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(5)(b): Upon completion of the orientation seminar described in Subsection (5)(a), the Judicial Council shall certify the justice court judge as qualified to hold office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(6)(a): The selection of a person to fill the office of justice court judge is effective upon certification of the judge by the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-202(6)(b): A justice court judge may not perform judicial duties until certified by the Judicial Council.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-203 Term of office for justice court judge -- Retention -- Reduction in force -- Addition of a justice court judge position.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-203(1): The term of a justice court judge is six years beginning the first Monday in January following the date of election.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-203(2): 20A-12-201; (2)(a) Upon the expiration of a justice court judge's term of office, the judge shall be subject to an unopposed retention election in accordance with the procedures set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-203(2)(a): in the county or counties in which the court to which the judge is appointed is located if the judge is a county justice court judge or a municipal justice court judge in a town or city of the fourth or fifth class; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-203(2)(b): (2)(a) in the municipality in which the court to which the judge is appointed is located if the judge is a municipal justice court judge and Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-203(3): Chapter 12, Judicial Performance Evaluation Commission Act Before each retention election, each justice court judge shall be evaluated in accordance with the performance evaluation program established in
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-203(4): A municipality or county that has more than one justice court judge and the weighted caseload per judge is lower than 0.60 as determined by the Administrative Office of the Courts may, at the municipality's or county's discretion and at the end of a judge's term of office, initiate a reduction in force and reduce, lay off, terminate, or eliminate a judge's position in accordance with the municipality's or county's employment policies.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-203(5): A municipality or county may only add a new justice court judge position if the Judicial Council, after considering the caseload of the court, approves creation of the position.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-204 Offices of justice court judges.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-204(1): Justice court judges holding office in:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-204(1)(a): county precincts are county justice court judges; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-204(1)(b): cities or towns are municipal justice court judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-204(2): The county legislative body may establish a single precinct or divide the county into multiple precincts to create county justice courts for public convenience.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-204(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-204(3)(a): The governing body may create as many judicial positions as are required for the efficient administration of a justice court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-204(3)(b): If more than one judge is assigned to a court, all filings within that court shall be assigned to the judges at random unless the governing body has been authorized to create specialized judicial calendars to serve the interests of justice.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-205 Required training -- Failure to attend.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-205(1): A justice court judge shall meet the continuing education requirements of the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-205(2): Successful completion of the continuing education requirement includes instruction regarding competency and understanding of constitutional provisions and laws relating to the jurisdiction of the court, rules of evidence, and rules of civil and criminal procedure as indicated by a certificate awarded by the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-205(3): The Judicial Council shall file a formal complaint with the Judicial Conduct Commission against each justice court judge who does not comply with this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206 Determination of compensation for justice court judge -- Limits on secondary employment -- Prohibition on holding political or elected office -- Penalties.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(1): (1)(a); (1)(b)(ii); (1)(a); (1)(c); (1); 78A-7-209.5 Every justice court judge shall be paid a fixed compensation determined by the governing body of the respective municipality or county.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(1)(a): The governing body of the municipality or county may not set a full-time justice court judge's salary at less than 70% nor more than 90% of a district court judge's salary.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(1)(b): (1)(a); (1)(b)(ii); (1)(a) The governing body of the municipality or county shall set a part-time justice court judge's salary as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(1)(b)(i): (1)(a) The governing body shall first determine the full-time salary range outlined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(1)(b)(ii): The caseload of a part-time judge shall be determined by the office of the state court administrator and expressed as a percentage of the caseload of a full-time judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(1)(b)(iii): (1)(b)(ii); (1)(a) The judge's salary shall then be determined by applying the percentage determined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(1)(c): A justice court judge shall receive an annual salary adjustment at least equal to the average salary adjustment for all county or municipal employees for the jurisdiction served by the judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(1)(d): (1)(c) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(1)(e): A justice court judge employed by more than one entity as a justice court judge may not receive a total salary for service as a justice court judge greater than the salary of a district court judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(1)(f): (1); 78A-7-209.5 A salary described in this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(2): A justice court judge may not appear as an attorney in any:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(2)(a): justice court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(2)(b): criminal matter in any federal, state, or local court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(2)(c): juvenile court case involving conduct which would be criminal if committed by an adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(3): A justice court judge may not hold any office or employment including contracting for services in any justice agency of state government or any political subdivision of the state including law enforcement, prosecution, criminal defense, corrections, or court employment.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(4): A justice court judge may not hold any office in any political party or organization engaged in any political activity or serve as an elected official in state government or any political subdivision of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(5): A justice court judge may not own or be employed by any business entity which regularly litigates in small claims court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-206(6): The Judicial Council shall file a formal complaint with the Judicial Conduct Commission for each violation of this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-208 Temporary justice court judge.
--------------------------------------------------------------
When necessary, the governing body may appoint any senior justice court judge, or justice court judge currently holding office within the judicial district or in an adjacent county, to serve as a temporary justice court judge.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5 Presiding judge -- Associate presiding judge -- Election -- Powers -- Duties.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(1): 78A-7-301
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(1)(a): In judicial districts having more than one justice court judge, the justice court judges shall elect one judge of the district to the office of presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(1)(b): 78A-7-301 The presiding judge shall receive an additional $2,000 per annum as compensation from the Justice Court Technology, Security, and Training Account described in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(2)(b): 78A-7-301 The associate presiding judge shall receive an additional $1,000 per annum as compensation from the Justice Court Technology, Security, and Training Account described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3): 78A-7-208; 78A-7-208; 78A-7-202 The presiding judge has the following authority and responsibilities, consistent with the policies of the Judicial Council:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(a): working with each justice court judge in the district to implement policies and rules of the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(b): exercising powers and performing administrative duties as authorized by the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(c): if there is no other appointed justice court judge in that court available, assigning a justice court judge to hear a case in which a judge has been disqualified in accordance with rules of the Supreme Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(d): 78A-7-208; 78A-7-208; 78A-7-202 if a justice court judge of the district cannot perform the justice court judge's duties in a case or cases due to illness, death, or other incapacity, and the governing body has not appointed a temporary justice court judge in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(d)(i): assigning, on an emergency basis, a justice court judge to hear a case or cases; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(d)(ii): 78A-7-208; 78A-7-202 facilitating judicial coverage with the appointing municipal or county authority until a temporary justice court judge can be appointed, in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(e): entering orders of expungement in cases expunged in accordance with Title 77, Chapter 40a, Part 2, Automatic Expungement and Deletion.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(4)(a): When the presiding judge is unavailable, the associate presiding judge shall assume the responsibilities of the presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(4)(b): The associate presiding judge shall perform other duties assigned by the presiding judge.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5 Presiding judge -- Associate presiding judge -- Election -- Powers -- Duties.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(1): 78A-7-301

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(2): 78A-7-301
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(2)(a): In judicial districts having more than two justice court judges, the justice court judges may elect one judge of the district to the office of associate presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(2)(b): 78A-7-301 The associate presiding judge shall receive an additional $1,000 per annum as compensation from the Justice Court Technology, Security, and Training Account described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3): 78A-7-208; 78A-7-208; 78A-7-202 The presiding judge has the following authority and responsibilities, consistent with the policies of the Judicial Council:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(a): working with each justice court judge in the district to implement policies and rules of the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(b): exercising powers and performing administrative duties as authorized by the Judicial Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(c): if there is no other appointed justice court judge in that court available, assigning a justice court judge to hear a case in which a judge has been disqualified in accordance with rules of the Supreme Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(d): 78A-7-208; 78A-7-208; 78A-7-202 if a justice court judge of the district cannot perform the justice court judge's duties in a case or cases due to illness, death, or other incapacity, and the governing body has not appointed a temporary justice court judge in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(d)(i): assigning, on an emergency basis, a justice court judge to hear a case or cases; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(d)(ii): 78A-7-208; 78A-7-202 facilitating judicial coverage with the appointing municipal or county authority until a temporary justice court judge can be appointed, in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(3)(e): entering orders of expungement in cases expunged in accordance with Title 77, Chapter 40a, Part 2, Automatic Expungement and Deletion.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(4)(a): When the presiding judge is unavailable, the associate presiding judge shall assume the responsibilities of the presiding judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-209.5(4)(b): The associate presiding judge shall perform other duties assigned by the presiding judge.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-210 Justice court judge administrative responsibilities.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-210(1): Justice court judges shall comply with and ensure that court personnel comply with applicable county or municipal rules and regulations related to personnel, budgets, and other administrative functions.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-210(2): Failure by the judge to comply with applicable administrative county or municipal rules and regulations may be referred, by the county executive or municipal legislative body, to the state Justice Court Administrator.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-210(3): Repeated or willful noncompliance may be referred, by the county executive or municipal legislative body, to the Judicial Conduct Commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-212 Place of holding court.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-212(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-212(1)(a): County justice court judges may hold court in any municipality within the precinct but may exercise only the jurisdiction provided by law for county justice courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-212(1)(b): County justice court judges may also, at the direction of the county legislative body, hold court anywhere in the county as needed but may only hear cases arising within the precinct.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-212(2): A municipal justice court judge shall hold court in the municipality where the court is located and, as directed by the municipal governing body, at the county jail or municipal prison.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213 Trial facilities -- Hours of business.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(1): A justice court judge shall conduct all official court business in a courtroom or office located in a public facility which is conducive and appropriate to the administration of justice.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(2)(a): A county justice court may, at the direction of the county legislative body, hold justice court anywhere in the county as needed but may only hear cases arising within its precinct.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(2)(b): A municipal justice court judge shall hold court in the municipality where the court is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(2)(c): Justice courts may also hold court or conduct hearings or court business in any facility or location authorized by rule of the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(3): Justice courts shall be open and judicial business shall be transacted:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(3)(a): five days per week; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(3)(b): no less than four days per week for at least 11 hours per day.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(4): (3) The legislative body of the county, city, or town shall establish operating hours for the justice courts within the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(5): The hours the courts are open shall be posted conspicuously at the courts and in local public buildings.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(6): The clerk of the court and judges of justice courts shall attend the court at regularly scheduled times.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-213(7): By July 1, 2011, all justice courts shall use a common case management system and disposition reporting system as specified by the Judicial Council.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-215 Monthly reports to court administrator and governing body.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-215(1): Every justice court shall file monthly with the state court administrator a report of the judicial business of the judge.  The report shall be on forms supplied by the state court administrator.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-215(2): The report shall state the number of criminal and small claims actions filed, the dispositions entered, and other information as specified in the forms.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-215(3): A copy of the report shall be furnished by the justice court to the person or office in the county, city, or town designated by the governing body to receive the report.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-301 Justice Court Technology, Security, and Training Account established -- Funding -- Uses.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-301(1): There is created a restricted account in the General Fund known as the Justice Court Technology, Security, and Training Account.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-7-301(2): 78A-7-122(4)(b)(iii); 77-2-4.2(5); (6) The state treasurer shall deposit in the account:

Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Chapter 8 - Small Claims Courts
*****************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-101 Creation.
-----------------------------------------
There is created a limited jurisdiction division of the district and justice courts designated small claims court.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102 Small claims -- Defined -- Counsel not necessary -- Removal from district court -- Deferring multiple claims of one plaintiff -- Supreme Court to govern procedures.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(1): (1)(a)(i) A small claims action is a civil action:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(1)(a): for the recovery of money when:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(1)(a)(i): the amount claimed does not exceed:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(1)(a)(i)(A): on or after May 4, 2022, through December 31, 2024, $15,000 including attorney fees but exclusive of court costs and interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(1)(a)(i)(B): on or after January 1, 2025, through December 31, 2029, $20,000 including attorney fees but exclusive of court costs and interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(1)(a)(i)(C): on or after January 1, 2030, $25,000 including attorney fees but exclusive of court costs and interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(1)(a)(ii): the defendant resides or the action of indebtedness was incurred within the jurisdiction of the court in which the action is to be maintained; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(1)(b): (1)(a)(i) involving interpleader under Rule 22 of the Utah Rules of Civil Procedure, in which the amount claimed does not exceed the amount described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(2): (1)(a)(i); (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(2)(a): (1)(a)(i) A defendant in an action filed in the district court that meets the requirement of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(2)(a)(i): giving notice, including the small claims filing number, to the district court of removal during the time afforded for a responsive pleading; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(2)(a)(ii): paying the applicable small claims filing fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(2)(b): (2)(a) A filing fee may not be charged to a plaintiff to appeal a judgment on an action removed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(3): (1)(a)(i) The judgment in a small claims action may not exceed the amount described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(4): A counter claim may be maintained in a small claims action if the counter claim arises out of the transaction or occurrence which is the subject matter of the plaintiff's claim.  A counter claim may not be raised for the first time in the trial de novo of the small claims action.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(5)(a): A claim involving property damage from a motor vehicle accident may be maintained in a small claims action, and any removal or appeal of the small claims action, without limiting the ability of a plaintiff to make a claim for bodily injury against the same defendant in a separate legal action.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(5)(b): In the event that a property damage claim is brought as a small claims action:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(5)(b)(i): a liability decision in an original small claims action or appeal of the original small claims action is not binding in a separate legal action for bodily injury; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(5)(b)(ii): an additional property damage claim may not be brought in a separate legal action for bodily injury.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(6)(a): With or without counsel, persons or corporations may litigate actions on behalf of themselves:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(6)(a)(i): in person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(6)(a)(ii): through authorized employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(6)(b): A person or corporation may be represented in an action by an individual who is not an employee of the person or corporation and is not licensed to practice law only in accordance with the Utah Rules of Small Claims Procedure as made by the Supreme Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(7)(a): If a person or corporation other than a municipality or a political subdivision of the state files multiple small claims in any one court, the clerk or judge of the court may remove all but the initial claim from the court's calendar in order to dispose of all other small claims matters.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(7)(b): A claim so removed shall be rescheduled as permitted by the court's calendar.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-102(8): A small claims matter shall be managed in accordance with simplified rules of procedure and evidence made by the Supreme Court.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-103 Assignee may not file claim.
------------------------------------------------------------
A claim may not be filed or prosecuted in small claims court by any assignee of a claim.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-104 Object of small claims -- Attachment, garnishment, and execution.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-104(1): The hearing in a small claims action has the sole object of dispensing speedy justice between the parties.  The record of small claims proceedings shall be as provided by rule of the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-104(2): Attachment, garnishment, and execution may issue after judgment as prescribed by law, upon the payment of the fees required for those services.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-105 Civil filing fees.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-105(1): 78A-2-301 Except as provided in this section, the fees for a small claims action in justice court shall be the same as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-105(2): Fees collected in small claims actions filed in municipal justice court are remitted to the municipal treasurer.  Fees collected in small claims actions filed in a county justice court are remitted to the county treasurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-105(3): The fee in the justice court for filing a notice of appeal for trial de novo in a court of record is $10.  The fee covers all services of the justice court on appeal but does not satisfy the trial de novo filing fee in the court of record.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-106 Appeals -- Who may take and jurisdiction.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-106(1): Either party may appeal the judgment in a small claims action to the district court of the county by filing a notice of appeal in the original trial court within 28 days of entry of the judgment.  If the judgment in a small claims action is entered by a judge or judge pro tempore of the district court, the notice of appeal shall be filed with the district court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-106(2): 78A-8-108 The appeal is a trial de novo and shall be tried in accordance with the procedures of small claims actions.  A record of the trial shall be maintained.  The trial de novo may not be heard by a judge pro tempore appointed under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-107 Costs.
--------------------------------------
The prevailing party in any small claims action is entitled to costs of the action and also the costs of execution upon a judgment rendered therein.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-108 Evening hours -- Judges pro tempore.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-108(1): The district or justice court may request that the Supreme Court appoint a member of the Utah State Bar in good standing, with the member's consent, as judge pro tempore to hear and determine small claims at times, including evening sessions, to be set by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-108(2): After being duly sworn, judges pro tempore shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-108(2)(a): serve voluntarily and without compensation at the request of the court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-108(2)(b): be extended the same immunities, and have the same powers with respect to matters within the jurisdiction of the small claims court as exercised by a regular judge.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-8-109 Report to Judiciary Interim Committee.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
The Judicial Council shall present to the Judiciary Interim Committee, if requested by the committee, a report and recommendation concerning the maximum amount of small claims actions.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Chapter 9 - Attorneys
*******************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-101 Admission to state bar -- Criminal history background checks.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-101(1): The Utah State Bar shall require each person applying for admission to the Utah State Bar to submit a complete set of fingerprints for the purpose of conducting a national criminal history background check.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-101(2): Fingerprints of applicants for admission to the Utah State Bar shall be submitted to the Department of Public Safety, Bureau of Criminal Identification to be used to conduct a criminal history background check and to the Federal Bureau of Investigation to obtain a national criminal history background check.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-101(3): The criminal history background information obtained from the Department of Public Safety and the national criminal history background information obtained from the Federal Bureau of Investigation pursuant to this section may be used by the Utah State Bar to determine an applicant's character, fitness, and suitability for admission to the Utah State Bar.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-102 Fees for certificate of admission.
------------------------------------------------------------------
The appellate courts shall receive a $50 fee for a certificate of admission as attorney and counselor, $30 of which shall be distributed by the state treasurer to the Judicial Council as a dedicated credit for the benefit of the State Law Library.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-103 Practicing law without a license prohibited -- Exceptions.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-103(1): Unless otherwise provided by law or court rule, an individual may not practice law or assume to act or hold himself or herself out to the public as an individual qualified to practice law within this state if that individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-103(1)(a): is not admitted and licensed to practice law within this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-103(1)(b): has been disbarred or suspended from the practice of law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-103(1)(c): is prohibited from practicing law by court order entered pursuant to the courts' inherent powers or published court rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-103(2): (1) The prohibition against the practice of law described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-9-103(3): Nothing in this section prohibits an individual from personally and fully representing that individual's own interests in a cause to which that individual is a party in the individual's own right and not as an assignee.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203 Procedures for judicial nomination commission -- Meetings -- Certification -- Governor appointment.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(1): Title 52, Chapter 4, Open and Public Meetings Act
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(1)(a): A commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(1)(a)(i): meet as necessary to perform the commission's function; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(1)(a)(ii): investigate the applicants of a judicial vacancy, including seeking input from members and employees of the judiciary and the community.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(1)(b): A commission may consult with the Judicial Council regarding the applicants for a judicial vacancy.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(1)(c): Title 52, Chapter 4, Open and Public Meetings Act A commission is exempt from the requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(2): In determining which of the applicants are the most qualified, a commission shall determine by a majority vote of the commissioners present which of the applicants best possess the ability, temperament, training, and experience that qualifies an applicant for the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(3): (3)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(3)(a): (3)(b) Except as provided under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(3)(a)(i): the appellate court nominating commission shall certify to the governor a list of the seven most qualified applicants per judicial vacancy;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(3)(a)(ii): a district and juvenile court nominating commission shall certify to the governor a list of the five most qualified applicants per judicial vacancy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(3)(a)(iii): the business and chancery court nominating commission shall certify to the governor a list of the seven most qualified applicants per judicial vacancy.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(3)(b): If a commission is considering applicants for more than one judicial vacancy existing at the same time and for the same court, the commission shall include one additional applicant for each additional judicial vacancy in the court in the list of applicants the commission certifies to the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(4): (3); 78A-10a-202 A commission shall certify a list to the governor under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(5): A commission shall, at the time that the commission certifies a list of the most qualified applicants to the governor, submit the same list to the president of the Senate, the Senate minority leader, and the Office of Legislative Research and General Counsel.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(6): A commission shall ensure that the list of applicants certified to the governor:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(6)(a): meet the qualifications required by law to fill the office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(6)(b): are willing to serve.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(7): In determining which of the applicants are the most qualified, a commission may not decline to certify an applicant's name to the governor because:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(7)(a): the commission declined to submit that applicant's name to the governor to fill a previous judicial vacancy;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(7)(b): a previous commission declined to submit that applicant's name to the governor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(7)(c): the commission or a previous commission submitted the applicant's name to the governor and the governor selected another individual to fill the judicial vacancy.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(8): A commission may not certify:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(8)(a): an applicant who is a justice or judge that was not retained by the voters for the office for which the justice or judge was defeated until after the expiration of that justice's or judge's term of office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(8)(b): an applicant who has served on a commission within six months after the day on which the commission was last convened.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(9): The governor shall fill a judicial vacancy within 30 days after the day on which the governor received the list of nominees from the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-203(10): If the governor fails to fill a judicial vacancy within 30 days after the day on which the governor received the list of nominees from the commission, the chief justice of the Supreme Court shall, within 20 days, appoint an applicant from the list of nominees certified to the governor by the commission.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-204 Senate confirmation of judicial appointments for courts of record.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-204(1): The Senate shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-204(1)(a): consider and render a decision on each judicial appointment within 60 days after the day of the judicial appointment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-204(1)(b): if necessary, convene the Senate in an extraordinary session to consider the judicial appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-204(2): If the Senate fails to approve a judicial appointment, the office is considered vacant and a new nominating process begins.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-204(3): A judicial appointment is effective upon approval of a majority of all members of the Senate.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-301 Definitions.
----------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-301(1): 78A-10a-302 "Commission" means the Appellate Court Nominating Commission created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-301(2): 78A-10a-302 "Commissioner" means an individual appointed by the governor to serve on the Appellate Court Nominating Commission created under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-302 Creation -- Purpose.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-302(1): There is created the Appellate Court Nominating Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-302(2): The Appellate Court Nominating Commission shall nominate individuals to fill judicial vacancies on the Supreme Court and the Court of Appeals.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303 Membership -- Vacancies -- Removal.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(1): The Appellate Court Nominating Commission shall consist of seven commissioners, each appointed by the governor to serve a four-year term.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(2): A commissioner shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(2)(a): be a United States citizen;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(2)(b): be a resident of Utah; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(2)(c): serve until the commissioner's successor is appointed.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(3): The governor may not appoint:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(3)(a): a commissioner to serve successive terms; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(3)(b): a member of the Legislature to serve as a commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(4): In determining whether to appoint an individual to serve as a commissioner, the governor shall consider whether the individual's appointment would ensure that the commission selects applicants without any regard to partisan political consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(5): The governor shall appoint the chair of the commission from among the membership of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(6): The governor shall fill any vacancy on the commission caused by the expiration of a commissioner's term.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(7): (7)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(7)(a): If a commissioner is disqualified, removed, or is otherwise unable to serve, the governor shall appoint a replacement commissioner to fill the vacancy for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(7)(b): (7)(a) A replacement commissioner appointed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-10a-303(8): The governor may remove a commissioner from the commission at any time with or without cause.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 78A - Chapter 11 - Judicial Conduct Commission
**************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-101 Creation.
------------------------------------------
In accordance with Article VIII, Section 13 of the Utah Constitution, a Judicial Conduct Commission is created.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-102(1): "Commission" means the Judicial Conduct Commission established by Utah Constitution Article VIII, Section 13, and this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-102(2)(a): "Complaint" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-102(2)(a)(i): a written complaint against a judge; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-102(2)(a)(ii): an allegation based on reliable information received in any form, from any source, that alleges, or from which a reasonable inference can be drawn that a judge is in violation of any provision of Utah Constitution Article VIII, Section 13.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-102(2)(b): "Complaint" does not include an allegation initiated by the commission or its staff.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-102(3): "Investigation" means an inquiry into an allegation of misconduct, including a search for and examination of evidence concerning the allegations, which begins upon the receipt of a complaint and is completed when either the complaint is dismissed by a majority vote of the commission or when an order is sent to the Supreme Court for its review in accordance with Utah Constitution Article VIII, Section 13.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-102(4): "Judge" includes the chief justice of the Supreme Court, a justice of the Supreme Court, a judge of the Court of Appeals, a judge of the Business and Chancery Court, a district court judge, an active senior judge, a juvenile court judge, a justice court judge, an active senior justice court judge, and a judge pro tempore of any court of this state.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103 Judicial Conduct Commission -- Members -- Terms -- Vacancies -- Voting -- Power of chair.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1)(a): The membership of the commission consists of the following 11 members:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1)(a)(i): two members of the House of Representatives to be appointed by the speaker of the House of Representatives for a four-year term, not more than one of whom may be of the same political party as the speaker;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1)(a)(ii): two members of the Senate to be appointed by the president of the Senate for a four-year term, not more than one of whom may be of the same political party as the president;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1)(a)(iii): two members of, and in good standing with, the Utah State Bar, who shall be appointed by a majority of the Utah Supreme Court for a four-year term, none of whom may reside in the same judicial district;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1)(a)(iv): three persons not members of the Utah State Bar, who shall be appointed by the governor, with the advice and consent of the Senate, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 24, Part 2, Vacancies, for four-year terms, not more than two of whom may be of the same political party as the governor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1)(a)(v): subject to Subsection (1)(b), two judges to be appointed by a majority of the Utah Supreme Court for a four-year term.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1)(b): The two judges appointed under Subsection (1)(a)(v) may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1)(b)(i): be a member of the Utah Supreme Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1)(b)(ii): serve on the same level of court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(1)(b)(iii): serve primarily in the same judicial district if the judges are district or juvenile court judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(2)(a): The terms of the members shall be staggered so that approximately half of the commission expires every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(2)(b): Members of the commission may not serve longer than eight years.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(3): The commission shall establish guidelines and procedures for the disqualification of any member from consideration of any matter.  A judge who is a member of the commission or the Supreme Court may not participate in any proceedings involving the judge's own removal or retirement.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(4)(a): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the applicable appointing authority shall, in accordance with any procedure described in this section, appoint a replacement for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(4)(b): If the appointing authority fails to appoint a replacement, the commissioners who have been appointed may act as a commission under all the provisions of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(5): Six members of the commission shall constitute a quorum.  Any action of a majority of the quorum constitutes the action of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(6): 78A-11-102
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(6)(a): 78A-11-102 At each commission meeting, the chair and executive director shall schedule all complaints to be heard by the commission and present any information from which a reasonable inference can be drawn that a judge has committed misconduct so that the commission may determine by majority vote of a quorum whether the executive director shall draft a written complaint in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(6)(b): The chair and executive director may not act to dismiss any complaint without a majority vote of a quorum of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(6)(c): A member of the commission described in Subsection (1)(a)(iv) shall comply with the conflict of interest provisions described in Title 63G, Chapter 24, Part 3, Conflicts of Interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(7): It is the responsibility of the chair and the executive director to ensure that the commission complies with the procedures of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(8): The chair shall be nonvoting except in the case of a tie vote.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(9): The chair shall be allowed the actual expenses of secretarial services, the expenses of services for either a court reporter or a transcriber of electronic tape recordings, and other necessary administrative expenses incurred in the performance of the duties of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(10): Upon a majority vote of the quorum, the commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(10)(a): employ an executive director, legal counsel, investigators, and other staff to assist the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(10)(b): incur other reasonable and necessary expenses within the authorized budget of the commission and consistent with the duties of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-103(11): The commission shall make rules in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, outlining its procedures and the appointment of masters.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-104 Expenses -- Per diem and travel.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-104(1): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member who is not a legislator may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses as allowed in:

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105 Grounds for reprimand, censure, suspension, removal, or involuntary retirement of justice, judge, or justice court judge -- Suspension.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(1): The commission may issue an order, subject to the Supreme Court's review and issuance of a final order implementing, rejecting, or modifying the commission's order, that any judge be reprimanded, censured, suspended, removed from office, or involuntarily retired, for:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(1)(a): action which constitutes willful misconduct in office;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(1)(b): final conviction of a crime punishable as a felony under state or federal law;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(1)(c): willful and persistent failure to perform judicial duties;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(1)(d): disability that seriously interferes with the performance of judicial duties; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(1)(e): conduct prejudicial to the administration of justice which brings a judicial office into disrepute.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(2): (1) In addition to the reasons specified in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(3): 78A-2-221
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(3)(a): 78A-2-221 The Supreme Court may, on its own motion, suspend or remove a judge from office if the judge:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(3)(a)(i): develops a physical or mental disability that seriously interferes with the performance of his judicial duties as provided in the
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(3)(a)(ii): 78A-2-221 becomes unqualified to hold the judicial office as provided in the
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(3)(a)(iii): brings the judicial office into disrepute by engaging in conduct prejudicial to the administration of justice as provided in the
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-105(3)(b): The Supreme Court shall provide notice to the judge and an opportunity to be heard.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106 Criminal investigation of a judge -- Administrative leave.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(1)(a)(i): If the commission, during the course of its investigation into an allegation of judicial misconduct, receives information upon which a reasonable person might conclude that a misdemeanor or felony under state or federal law has been committed by a judge other than the chief justice of the Supreme Court, the commission shall immediately refer the allegation and any information relevant to the potential criminal violation to the chief justice of the Supreme Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(1)(a)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(1)(a)(ii)(A): Unless the allegation is plainly frivolous, the commission shall also immediately refer the allegation of criminal misconduct and any information relevant to the potential criminal violation to the local prosecuting attorney having jurisdiction to investigate and prosecute the crime.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(1)(a)(ii)(B): If the local prosecuting attorney receiving the allegation of criminal misconduct of a judge practices before that judge on a regular basis, or has a conflict of interest in investigating the crime, the local prosecuting attorney shall refer the allegation of criminal misconduct to another local or state prosecutor who would not have the same disability or conflict.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(1)(a)(ii)(C): The commission may concurrently proceed with its investigation of the complaint without waiting for the resolution of the criminal investigation by the prosecuting attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(1)(b): The chief justice of the Supreme Court may place a judge on administrative leave with or without pay if the chief justice has a reasonable basis to believe that the alleged crime occurred, that the judge committed the crime, and that the crime was either a felony or a misdemeanor which conduct may be prejudicial to the administration of justice or which brings a judicial office into disrepute.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(2): (1)(a)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(2)(a): (1)(a)(ii) If the commission, during the course of its investigation into an allegation of judicial misconduct, receives information upon which a reasonable person might conclude that a misdemeanor or felony under state or federal law has been committed by the chief justice of the Supreme Court, the commission shall immediately refer the allegation and any information relevant to the potential criminal violation to two justices of the Supreme Court and the local prosecuting attorney in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(2)(b): Two justices of the Supreme Court may place the chief justice of the Supreme Court on administrative leave with or without pay if the two justices have a reasonable basis to believe that the alleged crime occurred, that the chief justice committed the crime, and that the crime was either a felony or a misdemeanor which conduct may be prejudicial to the administration of justice or which brings a judicial office into disrepute.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(3): (1); (2); (1); (2); 49-17-301; 49-18-301; (4); (3)(b); 49-17-301; 49-18-301
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(3)(a): (1); (2); (1); (2) If a judge is or has been criminally charged or indicted for a class A misdemeanor or any felony under state or federal law and if the Supreme Court has not already acted under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(3)(b): 49-17-301; 49-18-301 The state court administrator shall, for the duration of the administrative leave, withhold all employer and employee contributions required under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(3)(c): (4); (3)(b); 49-17-301; 49-18-301 If the judge is not convicted of the criminal charge, and if after an investigation and final disposition of the case by the Judicial Conduct Commission, the judge is reinstated by the Supreme Court as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(4): The chief justice of the Supreme Court or two justices of the Supreme Court who ordered the judge on administrative leave shall order the reinstatement of the judge:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(4)(a): if the prosecutor to whom the allegations are referred by the commission determines no charge or indictment should be filed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-106(4)(b): after final disposition of the criminal case, if the judge is not convicted of a criminal charge and if the commission has not ordered the removal of the judge.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-107 Referral of attorney misconduct.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
If the commission, during the course of its investigation into an allegation of judicial misconduct, receives information upon which a reasonable person might conclude that a member of the state bar has violated one of the Rules of Professional Conduct, the commission shall refer that information about the attorney to the Office of Professional Conduct of the Utah State Bar.

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108 Involuntary disability retirement or removal of a judge.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108(1): The commission shall recommend and issue an order for the removal or involuntary retirement of a judge of any court of this state, in accordance with the procedure outlined in this section,  for a disability that seriously interferes with the performance of the judge's judicial duties and which is, or is likely to become, of a permanent character.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108(2): The commission shall order a medical examination and report.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108(3): The commission in recommending an order of involuntary retirement or removal of a judge for a disability, shall base it on the evaluation and recommendations submitted by one or more medical examiners or physicians, including an examination of essential statements submitted by either bar or judicial associations or committees certifying that:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108(3)(a): the judge acquires a physical or mental disability and this disability seriously interferes with the performance of the judge's judicial duties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108(3)(b): the judge's incapacity is likely to continue and be permanent and that the judge should be involuntarily retired or removed.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108(4)(a): The Supreme Court shall review the commission's proceedings as to both law and fact and may permit the introduction of additional evidence.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108(4)(b): After its review, the Supreme Court shall issue its order implementing, rejecting, or modifying the commission's order.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108(5): Retirement or involuntary retirement as provided in this chapter shall be processed through the Utah State Retirement Office, and the judge retiring shall meet the requirements for retirement as specified in this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-108(6): Upon an order for involuntary retirement, the judge shall retire with the same rights and privileges as if the judge retired pursuant to statute.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-109 Receipt of complaints.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-109(1): The commission shall receive and investigate any complaint against a judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-109(2): Unless the complaint alleges criminal misconduct, the commission may decline to investigate any complaint received four or more years after the act or omission which constitutes the alleged misconduct.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-109(3): During the course of any investigation, the commission may order a hearing to be held concerning the reprimand, censure, suspension, removal, or involuntary retirement of a judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-109(4): The commission shall provide the judge with all information necessary to prepare an adequate response or defense, which may include the identity of the complainant.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110 Hearing.
-----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(1)(a): A hearing may be conducted before a quorum of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(1)(b): Any finding or order shall be made upon a majority vote of the quorum.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(2): Alternatively, the commission may appoint three special masters, who are judges of courts of record, to hear and take evidence in the matter and to report to the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(3)(a): After the hearing or after considering the record and report of the masters, if the commission finds by a preponderance of the evidence that misconduct occurred, it shall order the reprimand, censure, suspension, removal, or involuntary retirement of the judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(3)(b): When a commission order is sent to the Supreme Court, it shall also be:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(3)(b)(i): publicly disclosed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(3)(b)(ii): sent to the entity that appointed the judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(3)(c): In recommending any order, including stipulated orders, the commission may not place, or attempt to place, any condition or limitation upon the Supreme Court's constitutional power to:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(3)(c)(i): review the commission's proceedings as to both law and fact; or
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(3)(c)(ii): implement, reject, or modify a commission order.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4): When the commission issues any order, including a stipulated order, that is sent to the Supreme Court, the record shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(a): the original complaint and any other information regarding violations, or potential violations, of the Code of Judicial Conduct;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(b): the charges;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(c): all correspondence and other documents which passed between the commission and the judge;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(d): all letters which may explain the charges;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(e): all affidavits, subpoenas, and testimony of witnesses;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(f): the commission's findings of fact and conclusions of law;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(g): a transcript of any proceedings, including hearings on motions;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(h): a copy of each exhibit admitted into evidence;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(i): a summary of all the complaints dismissed by the commission against the judge which contained allegations or information similar in nature to the misconduct under review by the Supreme Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(j): a summary of all the orders implemented, rejected, or modified by the Supreme Court against the judge; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-110(4)(k): all information in the commission's files on any informal resolution, including any letter of admonition, comment, or caution, that the commission issued against the judge prior to May 1, 2000.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-111 Supreme Court action.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-111(1): Before the implementation, rejection, or modification of any commission order the Supreme Court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-111(1)(a): review the commission's proceedings as to both law and fact and may permit the introduction of additional evidence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-111(1)(b): consider the number and nature of previous orders issued by the Supreme Court and may increase the severity of the order based on a pattern or practice of misconduct or for any other reason that the Supreme Court finds just and proper.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-111(2): After briefs have been submitted and any oral argument made, the Supreme Court shall issue its order implementing, rejecting, or modifying the commission's order.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-111(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-111(3)(a): Upon an order for removal, the judge shall be removed from office and his salary or compensation ceases from the date of the order.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-111(3)(b): Upon an order for suspension from office, the judge may not perform any judicial functions and may not receive a salary for the period of suspension.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-112 Confidentiality.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-112(1): 78A-11-110 The transmission, production, or disclosure of any complaints, papers, or testimony in the course of proceedings before the commission, the masters appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-112(2): 78A-11-110; 78A-11-106 The transmission, production, or disclosure of any complaints, papers, or testimony in the course of proceedings before the commission or the masters appointed under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-112(3)(a): upon order of the Supreme Court;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-112(3)(b): upon the request of the judge who is the subject of the complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-112(3)(c): (4) as provided in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-112(3)(e)(i): for information that has already been made public; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-112(3)(e)(ii): the final written and oral audit report of the Legislative Auditor General may present information about the commission as long as it contains no specific information that would easily identify a judge, witness, or complainant.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-112(4): If the Senate Judicial Confirmation Committee requests Judicial Conduct Commission records, the commission shall disclose the information to the Senate Judicial Confirmation Committee or its staff if the chair of the Senate Judicial Confirmation Committee certifies in writing that the committee will limit the disclosure of any information received to the minimum amount necessary to allow the Senate to evaluate the candidate's fitness for office.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-112(5): Upon the dismissal of a complaint or allegation against a judge, the dismissal shall be disclosed without consent of the judge to the person who filed the complaint.


Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-113 Subpoena power of the commission -- Testimony -- Contempt.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-113(1): The commission may issue subpoenas in aid of an investigation of a complaint filed with the commission.  The subpoena shall have the same authority as an order of the district court.  Commission subpoenas shall be issued in the manner and form prescribed for subpoenas by the Utah Rules of Civil Procedure.  Commission subpoenas shall be served in the manner prescribed for subpoenas by the Utah Rules of Civil Procedure.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-113(2): The commission may administer oaths and compel testimony under oath in aid of an investigation of a complaint filed with the commission and at hearings before the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-11-113(3): Title 78B, Chapter 6, Part 3, Contempt If a person fails to comply with a subpoena, or if a person appears before the commission and refuses to testify to a matter upon which the person may be lawfully questioned, the person is in contempt of the commission, and the commission may file in the district court a motion for an order to show cause why the penalties established in

Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201 Judicial Performance Evaluation Commission -- Creation -- Membership.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(1): There is created an independent commission called the Judicial Performance Evaluation Commission consisting of 13 members, as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(1)(a): two members appointed by the president of the Senate, only one of whom may be a member of the Utah State Bar;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(1)(b): two members appointed by the speaker of the House of Representatives, only one of whom may be a member of the Utah State Bar;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(1)(c): four members appointed by the members of the Supreme Court, at least one of whom, but not more than two of whom, may be a member of the Utah State Bar;
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(1)(d): four members appointed by the governor, at least one of whom, but not more than two of whom, may be a member of the Utah State Bar; and
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(1)(e): the executive director of the Commission on Criminal and Juvenile Justice.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(2): (1)(a); (b)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(2)(a): (1)(a); (b) The president of the Senate and the speaker of the House of Representatives shall confer when appointing members under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(2)(b): Each of the appointing authorities may appoint no more than half of the appointing authority's members from the same political party.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(2)(c): A sitting legislator or a sitting judge may not serve as a commission member.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(3): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(3)(a): (1) A member appointed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(3)(b): A member may serve no more than three consecutive terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(4): At the time of appointment, the terms of commission members shall be staggered so that approximately half of commission members' terms expire every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(5): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the replacement shall be appointed for the unexpired term by the same appointing authority that appointed the member creating the vacancy.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(6): (6)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(6)(a): Eight members of the commission constitute a quorum.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(6)(b): The action of a majority of the quorum constitutes the action of the commission, except that the commission may not make a determination that a judge meets or exceeds minimum performance standards, or that a judge does not meet or exceed minimum performance standards, by a vote of less than six members.
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(6)(c): (6)(b) If, because of absences, the commission is unable to make a determination described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 78A-12-201(6)(d): If a vote on the question of whether a judge meets or exceeds minimum performance standards or does not meet or exceed minimum performance standards ends in a tie or does not pass by at least six votes, the record shall reflect that the commission made no determination in relation to that judge.
